<Author>markt3
<Content>Almost Heaven No, I don't mean West Virginia. Visiting Scottsdale at this time of the year is just that - 'Heaven'. Temperatures are cool (40's) in the morning, but 70's by noon. The JW has everything a first class resort should have: excellent spa, 2 great golf courses, 4 super restaurants, conference rooms, banquet halls, pools and an in-house Starbucks. The room are comfortable and the beds are great, I actually slept very well on them. Service was impecciable, friendly and always helpful. We ate at 2 of the restaurants on site, Roy's, was had excellent food and Meritage, a steakhouse which had a wonderful $39 seasonal steak special. The lounge is very spacious, although somewhat noisy when crowded, but we spent a lot of our time at the outdoor fire pits in the evenings. We played the 'Palmer' golf course, which was very enjoyable and of course the desert vistas were wonderful. There is plenty of shopping and other types of less expensive restaurants nearby at the Desert Ridge outdoor mall-like area too.I would certainly return to JW Marriott Desert Ridge!

<Author>LeleW
<Content>Beautiful location, great spa, so-so room I had a conference at the Marriott this week and my husband scheduled some business meetings in Phoenix so he could join me. I'm a Marriott Rewards member and I'd read that the property was recently renovated, but our room was more rustic than nice -- and surprisingly dark. The bathroom was very small as well. Like most resorts in Phoenix, they claim to have a state of the art fitness center - but it's no big deal (e.g., no weight machines).The pluses - and there were many: The staff were unfailingly attentive; pretty much everyone asked if there was anything they could do for us. Also, housekeeping showed up one morning while we were still in the room and *immediately* offered to come back later. The fire pit area behind the restaurant is very nice to hang out at (especially in December, when even Phoenix can get a little chilly at night). Finally, the spa is beautiful - on a par with the Atlantic Resort in Fort Lauderdale, including a decent (although I wouldn't call even that one state of the art) fitness center -- but you have to pay $25 to visit (unless you schedule a service such as a massage). It also features a small, generally healthful restaurant (Sprouts) that's surprisingly reasonably priced for a resort spot -- AND has a nice little wine list and specialty drinks (e.g., a fresh raspberry juice mimosa).Upshot: A lovely venue with a great spa - but you don't want to spend too much time in your room.

<Author>BettyCrocker411
<Content>Surprisingly kid friendly but ditch the fees Our family of three (mom, dad and 7-year-old) really enjoyed the hotel. The staff for the most part were friendly and from all over the world. We met a young man from Kazakhstan on some exchange who was working in the restaurant. My guess is that the previous reviews about unfriendly staff had to do with English not being these people's first languages.The lazy river was surprisingly entertaining. We thought we would get bored going around and around but it was very relaxing -- a combination of people watching and going on a car ride.The rest of the pool complex had a little something for everybody. Even if I had a two-year-old and our elderly parents with us, there would have been pool stuff to enjoy for everybody.Our biggest complaint was the fees. The $13 fee for internet access is ridiculous, as is the $22 fee for valet parking, the $20 fee for access to the Revive Spa fitness center, the $20 for access to the golf driving range, the $20 access to the tennis facilities, etc. The parking lots are pretty far from the hotel and in the summer heat, it is not a pleasant walk.Why is it that at the lower end Marriott (Fairfield Inns), you get free breakfast and internet access but as you move up the price range all the freebies disappear? If you're shelling out a few hundred a night for accommodation the least they can give you is a free breakfast and internet access. Any management types listening?Fortunately, we got a really good hotel, air and car package through Southwest which made all the extra expenses reasonable in the big picture.

<Content>Going Downhill Since the resort opened, I have stayed at this location three times now. It seems the quality of service, with the exception of the hotel lobby and greeting staff, has gone downhill considerably. I was treated better at a Holiday Inn Express on my way to staying at the Desert Ridge Resort.To begin our stay, the new HDTV in our room did not work when connected to my laptop. Two technicians looked into the problem over two days, and basically dropped the ball. The issue was never resolved after the five night stay. The front desk apologized, but that was about it.In the hallways, the housekeeping staff did not acknowledge guests, did not smile, or wish them a Good Morning, say Hello, or anything of the like.The hotel is showing its age and needs to be maintained better. Carpets are worn, scuff marks are noticeable on the walls of the hotel's corridors, etc.The Lazy River closed at 7 PM in the summer! I find this difficult to believe since there was a good three to four hours more of decent cooler weather. In Phoenix, people like to be outside in the earlier mornings and late evenings. The schedule for this pool should be better than this. I was at conference all day, wanted to take a dip and was told to get out after 15 minutes. Ridiculous!On a separate occasion, I ordered two frozen drinks at the bar close to the Lazy River. The bartender did not even say hello or acknowledge my friend and I. We had to just give our drink orders. He charged us over $10 per drink which I think goes beyond gouging! He was rude and unfriendly. No tip for any of that!At the conference, a colleague of mine was served, not undercooked, but RAW chicken! We asked the staff member in charge to do something about it, but again, we received an unsatisfactory response.Is this the way to run a supposed resort?Then, there was the heavy sell job from the Marriott's Canyon Villas. As if I hadn't spent enough money in the place already! Are you kidding?I am tired of shelling out good money to be treated like this. I, for one, will not be returning to this hotel, and I will be avoiding JW Marriott hotels altogether.

<Author>dreampilot
<Content>Truly Mixed Feelings... Really Wanted to Like it ... But... We stayed here in mid July for six nights and seven days, four of those days attending a convention at the resort.We have a lot of mixed feelings and I have to say that if it wasn't for the great rate we got (nearly 70% off rack) because of our convention, we probably would rate this stay a lot lower. First the good...1. Location: It is convenient to the Desert Ridge marketplace, a full service mall including a 20 screen movie theater and dozens of restaurants. The Resort runs a shuttle every 15 minutes or so to the mall. If you have a rental car - it's location is very convenient to Phoenix's highway system and downtown is only 20 minutes away. 2. Grounds/Atmosphere: well kept - and you can't beat the bunny brigade as we called it. In the late afternoons, dozens of rabbits plop on the green grass and stretch out - it's an almost surreal experience which is fun for young and old alike. There is a lot of grounds to explore... Although I have to say Orlando's JW Marriott's lazy river is much more fun, there are at least more pools to choose from. The slide would be more fun if it wasn't turned off so early3. Rooms: Pretty typical for Marriott - which still has the best beds of most any hotel in it's tier. Bathrooms are nice and the flat screens come with full computer interface to hook up your laptops too. Patios in every room are a nice touch and big enough to host 4 friends relaxing.4. Front Desk Staff, Concierge, housekeeping and Parking Staff were great folks and easy to talk to and represented the Marriott brand wellNow the not so good...1. Service: Outside of the folks mentioned in #4 above, We were extremely disappointed in the service by the other staff. We had better experiences with service at Motel 6 and other budget brands then some of the people we ran into here at this JW. The lounge and bar staff were completely rude, hard to get a hold of and just not very pleasant people to deal with. Our waiter at Roys and one of our waiters at the Blue Sage were the rare exception to the restaurant staff as well. If I ever stay here again - I would much rather take a shuttle to Desert Ridge Marketplace and eat over there than waste any more money at the Resort restaurants and their rude service..2. Speaking of staff - the lack of friendliness at the pools by staff was also very noticeable - and quite honestly for what we're paying (if it was normal rack) - we would expect a few more options poolside for drinks and snacks similar to how Orlando's JW resort runs. 3. If you like the all in one contained resort experience, I suppose you will like the entertainment options (2 golf courses, spa, etc) available - but we made more trips into Phoenix than the average guest because quite frankly, these resorts can get boring and drain your pocketbook dry. So maybe in all fairness this complaint isn't fair to direct at this JW specifically - but imo, if you plan to stay a few days here consider renting a car (AT THE AIRPORT - NOT THE RESORT - YOULL SAVE LOTS OF MONEY) and exploring the area more.I am not overly picky about service but the consistent attitude and not so hot service we received from the lounge, restaurant and other staff here reduced our rating a whole star alone. Anyway - We would recommend this resort if you get a great deal but if you're paying full rate - you'd be much better off perhaps at another one of the many, many resort properties in the area.

<Author>tmalkoon
<Content>Beautiful Hotel-Lacks attention to detail We stayed here for 3 days at the beginning of July. We wanted to bring our 2 of our children to a resort with some water features. When we checked in I presented two $500 gift cards to put on our tab. I knew we would spend more than that and they need to be processed. The girl told us it would be more convenient to run them at check out. What she meant was it would be more convenient for her as they take some time to process. It was off putting to be turned down for payment up front. Also, I have used thousands of dollars of these in Marriotts across the country and have been greeted much more graciously.  One of the reasons we booked this hotel was for the lazy river and slide for our kids. The pools and grounds are gorgeous. We called before our trip and were told that the lazy river and slide were open until 7;00pm both nights so we booked it. However, both nights the river and slide stopped at 6:00 even though the signs posted said 7;00. Of course, the young people working the water area leave like robots as soon as it stopped flowing and couldn't answer any questions. We were later told that the features are on timer and a supervisor did not reset it. Our suite was $400 a night and there are many nice resorts in the Phoenix area with water features and better rates who are much more alert. It felt like the staff is less on top of things because there are fewer guests. Andrea at the front desk credited us $50 for the inconvience but the experience was not optimal.  On the plus side, our two room suite beautiful. The fabric and features are relaxing,upscale and the new LCD tv's were great. Another detail that fell through the cracks was the air conditioning in our suite. The kids side with the sleeper sofa was great, but our room with the king never cooled down(we set it at 60 but it was about 78) and it never went off the whole 3 days we were there. Again, management needs to pay more attention to the details.The Blue Sage restaurant on the property was great and the kids loved it. Our second night we left the pool and wanted to eat at Roys. They would not seat us because we were in our suits and cover ups. I could understand this during convention season in Phoenix. However, when it is 111 degrees, your restaurant is almost empty and there are only 2 resturants on the property that are open, it should be adjusted for the season. Again, property management should close for the summer or pay attention. Our general feeling is that this is a great corporate hotel in a beautiful setting. We are going to try another resort in Phoenix this summer but this one will not be it. If you are a family, there are much more welcoming and friendly options at a better price.

<Content>Beautiful Desert Oasis: Do not miss in Phoenix!!! This was my 3rd visit to Desert Ridge. The hotel is stunning. The property is large, well-maintained, relaxed and sophisticated. <Author>combatbalancer
<Content>What a fantastic resort For the last 10 years our March holiday has always been a Caribbean affair, taking in Antigua, Barbados, St Lucia, Canouan and Grenada which emerged as our favourite and resulted in 5 visits. The combination of almost guaranteed sunshine, sandy beaches, crystal clear seas and increasingly luxurious resort just had us coming back for more. But this year the combination of an early Easter and school holidays meant that redemption opportunities were nonexistent and discounted fares were very difficult to find.It was a friendwho said, Have you ever thought of going to Phoenix, Arizona?No. Never, was my reply. Seriously I thought Phoenix was wilderness USA, nothing but cattle ranches and cactuses. Nevertheless the seed had been sown and as I searched the internet I uncovered a raft of luxury resorts in the area, all brimming with swimming pools, golf courses, spas and other facilities. In fact it became clear that we could find everything we had become used to in the Caribbean apart from the sea. And since we adopted the little one - we have spent an increasing amount of time around the pool anyway. Award availability was wide open in all classes on the BA flights from LHR so we booked 3 Club seats and finally settled on the JW Marriott Desert Ridge Resort and Spa.Others we considered where the Phoenician (maybe a little more up market and very expensive), Fairmont Scottsdale Princess (it got lots of poor reviews for service), and the Royal Palm Resort (lovely but very few facilities for a 10 day stay). The Marriott won because it had 5 swimming pools, 6 restaurants, Two 18 hole golf courses, a spa, a desert botanical garden, expansive grounds, and a lazy river bigger than I have seen in most water parks I have visited.We arrived after a flawless flight and only 10 minutes to clear US customs and immigration, sweeping up this huge magestic driveway to be greeted by an army of bellhops and people eager to be at our beck and call. The reception of the hotel is set around a giant open plan Atrium area about 4 storeys high - a feature that apparantly is being introduced into Marriott resorts world wide. This provides a central meeting place for families, businessmen, and drinkers. It looks out onto an expansive lawn and lake called The Sage Lawn where we saw people playing ball games and later in the week special meals being served to conference delegates. Lining the lawn is the outside Vista Bar where they light the Firepits as soon as the sun goes down and these fires become the focal point for the evening live entertainment.Our standard room was very big - the king sized bed suitably covered in various layers of pillows, throws, wraps and other decorations. The bathroom had a walk in shower and spa bath and all the usual smelly stuff which they replaced twice everyday. There was a gigantic flat screen TV with all the usual pay for extra services. Great balcony patio with views over the desert and mountains. The swimming pool area was very impressive. 4 huge swimming pools (with a 5th available in the spa in a more private and tree lined location), and the lazy river. The latter was so relaxing - simple grab a huge rubber ring, sit back and be carried round a landscaped lap every 15 minutes or so. This was a good place for topping up the sun tan as well.We arrived on Easter Sunday and the resort was mobbed with families. On the first day the swimming pool area was very busy and I did have a fear that we had made a mistake (most Caribbean resorts have a very quiet relaxed air about them). But on the second day the families disappeared and the business conference delegates arrived so the swimming pool areas became very empty.The only thing I didn't like about the swimming pool area was the piped music - simply because it was intrusive. However they did have an extensive collection of 80s music and I heard songs like Safety Dance by Men Without Hats for the first time since the.....well since the 80s.The resort features some very impressive restaurants. Blue Sage - where you have a typical US breakfast and for the rest of the day typical US fare of burgers, steaks and ribs. Not the best place and the focal point for families but good value for breakfast.Roys - a Hawaiian Fusion restaurant with a great wine list which soon became our favourite. Sitting outside in their garden with torches burning and with the nearby firepits warming the air was a lovely setting. The Five Spice Fillet Steak melted like butter when cut and the rib starter was mouth watering. After dinner you can retire to lounge chairs around the firepit and finish of your bottle of red wine.Meritus Steak House - this was at the Golf Club and had an impressive range of steaks from NY Strip to their signature dish which is a smoked rib-eye steak - this was delicious - never had smoked beef before and it was a pleasant change from the normal way a steak gets cooked. Good squid and chicken here as well. Their terrace over looks the desert botantical garden and again is a lovely venue for an evening of food and wine.Tuscany - this is their signature restaurant and features gormet Italian fare. Another terrace garden, this time over looking a lake and The Isle of Capri which that night was being used for a conference dinner.The Spa - the restaurant here does fitness breakfasts and health conscious lunches. The spa itself is well equiped with a fitness studio for Yoga and Thai Chi, treatment rooms and a large swimming pool surrounded by palm trees and cabannas that you can hire out for a more relaxing day. Try the hot stone massage - quite deep and penetrating (oo - er!), and try walking on rubbery legs afterwards.Splash - is a poolside restaurant serving burgers and sandwiches. The turkey BLT was fabulous with waffle fries.Finally - not really a restaurant - but there was also a Starbucks and this had the longest queues. The yanks love their morning Starbucks don't they? We did breakfast - basically a grande and a muffin here several mornings.The grounds of the hotel were spotlessly clean, and liberally landscaped with waterfalls, lakes, flowers and cactuses. There were rabbits on the lawns and even mallard ducks swimming in the pools. And the coyotes came to the Golf course greens every evening. One night I even saw a barn owl swooping down over the roof of the golf club.Service everywhere was impeccable. Each bar and restaurant has plenty of waiting staff, people to pour more wine, people to clean up the plates and sometimes simply to have a chat - so it seemed.We took a day trip to the Grand Canyon which I am not even going to try and describe. It is one thing that only the eyes can appreciate. Photos and videos do not do the place justice. And we spent a morning riding horses in the desert. My first time on a horse and I enjoyed every minute of it - but boy was I sore the following day!!Any critisisms? Only one. The Hotel was very inconsistent with its turn down service. I find this at most hotels that offer it - including Ritz Carlton. If they are going to service the room for a second time during the day then they should be consistent. Some nights they only cleaned the bathroom, some they turned the bed down, put slippers by the bed, put a chocolate on the pillow and put on a soothing CD, other nights nothing at all. Anyway it resulted in a $100 credit when I made the comments.So I would whole heartedly recommend this place. We would go back definitely and as a winter holiday it gave us everything we have ever had in the Caribbean apart from the sea - but with one major major advantage. It is a dry arid climate so there are no biting insects. So for the first time in 10 years I didn't have to smother nuclear strength Deet Aftershave all over my body to stop a concerted mosquito attack.

<Author>paper11
<Content>Wonderful We just got back from this resort and we are talking about going again already. The resort was Beautiful and the staff was Wonderful. I don't think that I have stayed at another hotel that has had better all around customer service. Nearly every person we talked to, whether it was at different restaurants, outside, at the front desk etc. seemed genuinely happy and more than willing to answer any questions we had. Many members of the staff seemed to go out of there way to help. From the moment we got there, the staff outside were Very friendly. The first thing we did was eat lunch at an outside cafe and the waiter we had was Very nice. Later we had dinner and sat outside on the patio and listened to live music and our waitress was extremely nice and helpful. Another day, we went to the kid's play room that they have and the young woman there was one of the friendliest people I have ever met. Another day, we didn't get our roomed cleaned and someone came by to make sure we didn't need anything. We didn't, but it was nice that someone came by to ask. Another night, we had dinner at Roy's restaurant and the service was Excellent. We have a little one who has a few food restrictions due to allergies and they went out of their way to find her a dessert that she could eat (that came free with her meal) even after we told them it wasn't a big deal. Our little one loved the dessert!When we booked our vacation it came with a credit and room upgrade. The front desk was great at helping to make sure that we actually got these. The room was Great! We had a huge tub and stand up shower and a private balcony that we could sit on and listen to the live music each night. GREAT!!! We loved that. The entire resort was clean and the interior decorating throughout was beautiful. I appreciated all the of the details and decor everywhere. In your room you are also given a, What's going on today sheet that tells you everything you can participate in which is really nice. If I had to point out a few things that were not positive, there aren't many. There are many birds that fly around so there is a good number of bird droppings by the pool area and at least on the balcony that we had. But, you can walk around these. It doesn't take away at how beautiful the resort is and at how great the landscaping is. It's really beautiful. Although there is a lazy river, which is great fun and relaxing, if you have someone with you that cannot swim or isn't a strong swimmer, I wouldn't let them out of your sight. My husband, literally helped save a woman from drowning. She went up and down in and out of the water a couple times splashing around and when we realized she needed help, she had just went under water again and didn't resurface for many seconds with one hand sticking out of the water until my husband jumped in from the other side and got to her and pulled her out of the water. There was a lifeguard nearby, but I think she must not have seen her. Also, I think there are spots that the lifeguards cannot see and although the water isn't deep, it's moving and for someone who cannot swim well, it's easy to panic and slip which is what I think happened to this woman. Thankfully, she is ok. Also, I did have a couple drinks by the pool that were a little spendy that were not very good that I didn't finish, but then my husband and I both ordered a couple smoothies that we were delicious.Almost every staff member was friendly and we loved our vacation. We are talking about perhaps going to stay there again sometime!

<Author>sgordonosu
<Content>Great Spring Getaway My husband and I stayed here for 5 nights the first week of April. We had a fantastic time. We arrived at night and the hotel was beautifully lit. Upon entry the staff was very friendly and helpful. Walking to our room we were a little nervous as we had to walk to the back of the hotel and down the stairs. When we got into our room we were pleasantly surprised. The room was definitely one of the nicer rooms we have been in. Everything was very clean and updated. Our room had a small patio area that overlooked a water with a fountain. My husband is in sales and stays in hotel rooms across the country every week. He was impressed with the both the room and bathroom. The grounds of the hotel are spectacular. We found something new to explore every day we were there. We didn't find the pools to be too crowded. There are a variety of locations to sit at and enjoy the pools and waterfalls. We found the lazy river a nice place to sit near since it kept people moving by and not constantly splashing or yelling right in your face. There were also other locations through out the pool area that were quiet and relaxing just to sit and listen to the water falls. My husband is a Gold member and we had access to the spa fitness facility. Which was also very nice with ellipticals and tread mills with tv's attached as well as a variety of free weights and machines. The Desert Ridge mall is with in walking distance and offers a variety of great places to eat and shop.We at at Roy's one night which was fantastic. We had a lunch a few times at the pool and the staff was very accommodating. We had a great time seeing the wild life too. We made friends with a duck, got to see a nest of great horned owls at the spa and saw a variety of birds and bunnies. I was a bit nervous after reading some of the reviews. I do have to say some of them are a bit critical. My husband stays at various hotels across the U.S. every week. And he was very impressed with the grounds, room and service here. He pointed out that rarely does he find a hotel that has free internet access, few that have rooms that are as nice as these, and very few that have bathrooms as nice as this. Yes there are kids here and people enjoying their vacations, if that bothers you there are plenty of spaces around the 4 pools, hot tubs, lawns or spa that provide privacy.

<Author>CTSirTravelsAlot
<Content>Marriott, you can do MUCH better Recently returned from a 7 night stay (4/12-19) using Marriot Rewards points. This is my second stay at this hotel, last was 2 years ago for 3 nights.First, let me say I am a Gold Member of the Rewards program and am a loyal patron. That being said, I was dissapointed not to be treated like one. One week before check-in I requested a room overlooking the Desert Botanical Garden. I did this knowing that the rooms facing the pool are quite loud at times. I was told I had an upgraded view room.Upon check-in I was given a room with two over-sized Queens according to the front desk. Queens?? These are full beds and I am with my wife of nearly 15 years on vacation. Possibly we could have a King bed? Oh yes, and the room is on the 2nd floor overlooking...the pool. I called front desk immediately to let them know this was not satisfactory. They took my cell number and told me they would call when they had another room available.The time marched on until about 3:30. At this point, I was concerned they would have filled their rooms. I went to the front desk and found they only had 2 rooms left in the hotel. Unreal. They were a King on ground floor (I always request high floors, but apparently having that information in your Elite reservation status is just for one's own personal information) and another double/double room overlooking the Botanical Garden.I took the double/double begrudgingly as it least it had a decent view. By the way, no offer to help move my luggage...nice touch.Room we finally setlled in was standard for the resort. Nice view of mountains, botanical garden and....720 people from Bacardi on two mornings having breakfast. Now I dont begrudge the hotel for making money on corporate events, but they need a better system to make those on vacation not feel inconvenienced by these events. My inconvenience came at 3:30 AM on my 2nd night there when the staff started setting up the buffets, etc. Having come to AZ for the weather, I had my sliding glass door open. Ahhhh, the relaxing sounds of golf carts backing up (beep, beep, beeep) and rattling dishes, clanking glasses.Now, every day you get a sheet in your room with activities for the resort. Basically, this doesn't change form day to day. My suggestion? Put the events and location of events on their as a heads-up to the vacationing resort guests so they know if they should keep their door shut so as not to be awoken at 3:30 AM. Another thought, work it out with the corporation to give those in rooms overlooking their event a small gift. It would go a long way.Lastly, let's talk about litter. The grounds are mainly immaculate. This ends in the common areas outside, especially at the pools (SPA pool is worth the money). I know there are a huge number of people that traffic these areas, but the resort doesn't seem to know this. They need many more staff to clean up througout the day. Cups, straws, etc were everywhere. Part of the blame lay on the guests. Some of whom didn't make any effort to clean up after themselves. On the other hand, I shouldn't be swimming in a pool with empty cups at the bottom (at least 1 every day I was there). Also, as I was walking back to my room after a day at the pool and I noticed something striking. There was a sugar packet on the lawn as well as a piece of plastic. I saw 2 Marriott employees, one was dressed as a manager. I thought this will be interesting to see if they stop to pick up this trash. The answer? They walked right by. Marriott, train your employees to have pride in the resort surroundings. This is unacceptable.One last piece of advice: get some new chaise lounges out at the main pool. A number of them look like you got them from a garage sale. People are paying over $500 a night at this time of year for chairs like this? The lounges at the Spa should be standard for this kind of high-end resort.

<Content>Get A Discount or try elsewhere We stayed at the JW Marriott for three nights in April - it is a fairly new site and you could definately tell. The overall feel of the employees there was cold and, well, just plain rude. We were able to get a cheap rate - $125 per night - so we didn't feel to taken - but if you have to pay $300 or $400 for this place, look around somewhere else.

I have learned from my travels never to judge a book by the cover some of the wealthiest people in Scottsdale dress like gardners and drive  american cars! Here is my take on the JW Marriott. Great location but will not travel in March it is Spring Break and no matter where you travel whether beach or ski there will be plenty of kids about. I was suprised no one mentioned the vacation club time shares. Do not show interest when traveling past the time share desks because I did and not only had 3 separate voicemail messages on my room phone but also had a flyer put on my door so unless you are truly interested in their 90 min presentation steer clear. This hotel is located across from Desert Ridge Marketplace one of the cleanest outside shopping malls I have visited, it is not high end stores but has most everything moderate and they do provide a shuttle pick up from Desert Ridge. The rooms are some of the cleanest and the housekeeping staff very friendly. The pools were crowded due to the month of travel but there are several and they do clear out at 5:00 pm and since it is still very nice outside that is a great time for adults to attend.The restaurants are priced average for a hotel in this category. The room service prices are steep for breakfast so we went across to Mimi's or Paradise Bakery. Be prepared to walk alot, if you like to be near the pool or golf please ask to be near those areas. The nightly turndown service provides a schedule of activities for the next day, this is the first time I have seen a Segway tour offered. Overall a very pretty setting, quiet and very clean rooms. free parking, paid laundry room. As long as you like yellow and gold tones you will not be disappointed. Lots to do but you will pay for almost everything.

<Author>Surgie
<Content>Great stay at Desert Ridge! My husband and I were guests at the Marriott Desert Ridge from Mar. 24-29. Since we had an early morning flight, we had requested early check-in in advance. We knew it might or might not be available but we were happy to learn on arrival that our room was ready and it was only a little past 9:00 a.m. We had also requested a high floor in advance and we were given a room on the 5th floor (top floor) that overlooked the lagoon, golf course and mountains in the distance - very quiet and relaxing on the balcony.The room was spacious and nicely decorated. I have read other reviews complaining about the size of the room. We had a regular king room and there was a desk and chair, loveseat, coffee table, armoire and still plenty of room. I peeked in a room with 2 queens (or doubles) and it looked a little more cramped. So if a king bed suits your needs, you will find it more spacious. The bathroom was huge - separate tub and shower and large vanity.The staff went out of their way to be friendly and accommodating. The concierge made three dinner reservations for us, gave advice on activities we might enjoy, and printed out our boarding passes on the day of our check-out . Breakfast at the Blue Sage was great - good food and fast service - we ate outdoors each morning. We did not eat any other meals at the hotel so can't comment on that.Even though the hotel was full, the only place that seemed crowded was at the pool. It was somewhat of a chore to find a chair each day. Lots of chair-saving going on, even though the hotel says this is against their policy. However, the beverage service at the pool was fine. I forgot my pool wrist bracelet twice but this was not a problem - I had my room key and was not asked to go back to get the bracelet. I appreciate the staff's diligence in keeping outsiders out of the pool in order to keep it available for guests - this is common practice at other nice resorts.The spa was a real treat! It was expensive but in line with what other spas charge.I think when you travel at spring break, it takes a good attitude to have a great time and enjoy your vacation. Meeting people from different backgrounds is part of what makes travel so interesting if you're open-minded enough to appreciate it.

<Author>elliebear7
<Content>Not Impressed I was so excited to try out this property after reading some of the reviews and staying at other Marriott resorts but was disappointed with this one. Rooms okay (my lamp did not work either) but be sure and specifiy location, We literally had a balcony (with chairs) that overlooked the top of a building. I cannot begin to explain how horrible the view was. When I mentioned the view to the front desk I got a very fake smile and no response. Property is beautiful but provides none of the amenities of a top rate resort. Absolutely no internet access and not even a business center computer you can use without a charge (for gods sake Drury and Homewood Suites have business centers with internet access). I had to get a wrist band to use the pool so had to walk all the way back to the front desk (and believe me it is a walk). You had to ask for a towel, give your room number, wait while it was checked off and the attendant acted like he was doing me a favor by handing me a dirty looking towel. Again, two star hotels give pool access and towels with alot less trouble. Some of the employees looked genuinely happy to help (wait staff and housekeeping consistently good) but the front desk and pool folks were a different story. I would never pay full price for this hotel.

<Author>TessaTB
<Content>Best Experienced If You Come For The Outdoors We just got back from our vacation here and we had a great time using the pool facilities. The pool area is about the most impressive I've seen at a hotel. We had a blast, it's great if you have kids. Although it would be nice if they had an adult pool - dealing with all those children running around was annoying from time to time but we still had fun. They have an awesome golf course too. The hotel itself is very new money - a little bit gaudy and too done but impressive nonetheless. The entire resort is very pretty but also has the feeling of Orlando, FL because nothing looks natural. They had quite a few restaurants in different price ranges. We ate at Roy's twice and had a great time. The ambiance in there seemed the most fun, especially with the tiki torches. The room itself was disappointing for the amount of money you pay. It seems like they focused a lot on the outdoors and not so much in the rooms, they were pretty standard hotel rooms. It was nice to have a balcony though. We enjoyed the lounge area on the ground floor-they had live music every night we stayed which was great. They have fire pits all over the hotel grounds to sit around and warm up on cooler nights. Overall it was a fun stay but not quite worth all the money.

<Content>Great place for a conference I stayed here March 13-16 for a conference. The room I stayed in was huge with a king bed and a pull out sofa. The other one (for which you pay) was in the Spa...it looked much nicer, but I didn't feel the need to have to use my money to go there.Food at the conference was very good. <Author>MTVandendooren
<Content>What about the rooms?! Our family recently spent 2 nights at this hotel. Yes, the property is VERY nice - we paid a lot to stay, so that is to be expected. The negatives, however, speak for themselves. Firstly, the room itself was unimpressive in terms of decor/size, disappointing given the cost, but not a huge deal. Secondly, the FAN! The fan in our room was so incredibly noisy buzzing and clicking on and off, that we had to get up in the middle of the night to switch it off. Consequently, we had to sleep without air conditioning in an overly warm and stuffy room. Thirdly, we asked for a golf course view, and could juuuuuust barely make it out from our balcony on the 2nd floor of the hotel. We called and asked for a higher room, and were told they were 'fully committed', and that we couldn't have another room. Hard to believe given the hallways, restaurants, and pool areas were not busy at all during our stay. Fourth, the curtains did NOT cover the windows! That is, the curtain stopped at 1/4 of the way across the window, so we got full sunlight every morning, much to our dismay. And fifth, the music that they play in the pool area, courtyard etc., is soft and lovely..but it started each morning at 5AM! Do they really need to pump musak at 5AM!? Needless to say, it woke us up... The positives are that the staff were nice, the hotel itself is lovely, and the spa was great. I really wish they'd put more thought into the rooms - very disappointing. We had to go home to get a good nights' sleep. :(

<Content>Something missing Arriving at the J.W. Marriott I was impressed by the entrance and beauty of the building and landscaping. My room was ready and check in was quick and easy. It is a walk to everywhere. The room was smaller than I expected. Is there a special on throw pillows. The bathroom was very appealing. However, a 29 in TV, you're kidding me. This is a resort, I don't even have 29 in tvs at home. There was no DVD player in the room which I would have expected. The rooms were also a little noisy for my taste. The grounds and facilities are stunning with the exception of the health club, which is mediocre. Why is it that Resort and Spas usually have poor health clubs? Maybe the belief is you're here to be lazy, if you want to sweat, go to Bally's The equipment was in bad condition and it just wasn't a good facility. The health club requires you to walk outside to get there (bad move). The pools were beautiful with a lazy river and walking path along side.The hotel is pretty isolated, but it is located in a relatively nice area with a huge shopping complex and strip mall within walking distance. We always ate dinner offsite at one of the restaurants, so I didn't have a chance to eat at the Resort. My wife said the Spa was first class and thought the prices were reasonable. There is also a golf course on the grounds (it's Phoenix). I would stay here again, but it probably wouldn't be my first choice in the Phoenix area. I've stayed in much better rooms for less money and better looking places. My wife and I went for a convention and spent a couple of extra days, but as soon we were leaving, another convention was moving in. Maybe that had to do with the coldness of the place. That may be what's missing.

<Content>Lived Up to High Expectations We were here for a 4 day weekend (President's Day) and had a great time! The rooms are large and the bathrooms spacious with nice amenities. The hotel offers a variety of recreational activites-spa, golf, tennis, pool, variety of restaurants. After reading some other reviews, our main concern prior to our visit was whether the hotel is relaxing or a convention hotel with a rude and noisy expense account crowd dominating. During our visit several groups had meetings but none seemed to interfer with the guests who were just there to relax. <Author>Gracie27
<Content>Classy Place We went out to Phoenix for a girls spa trip from 2/15 through 2/18-just a quick weekend getaway. This hotel was wonderful-the grounds are beautiful, the staff is so helpful, the spa was one of the nicest I have ever been to, and the food was excellent. I will say they definetely focus on their conventions and it is a great resort for golfers...if you are looking to experience downtown Phoenix, I wouldn't recommend this place but for a nice, relaxing trip, convention, or golf outing, its perfect. We spent a lot of time across the street at the Desert Ridge Marketplace, eating and shopping and the Resort offers a complimentary shuttle service back and forth as well.Our room was on the top floor overlooking the front of the hotel-it was the perfect size for the three of us. And honestly the only complaint i have was that during the evening you could hear the lobby band playing from our room because the main hotel is set up like an atrium so many rooms overlook the lobby and noise carries, but we just put the tv on and went to sleep and it stopped at a decent hour, so it really wasn't a pain. The hotel was beautiful, I loved how they have the fruited water all over the place and they gave you a free starbucks coffee coupon every morning. They had nature walks along the trails and the fitness center was very nice (no one was really there). Besides the spa cafe, we did not eat at any of the restaurants in the hotel so I cannot comment on them. I would love to come back to this resort when its a little warmer and I can really enjoy the pool. Hope this helps.

<Author>ScipioAfricanus
<Content>Institutional, Great Service, But Convention Oriented Hotel This is a huge, institutional convention resort. This is not a cozy place. It's huge and impersonal. The service was some of the best I've experienced in recent memory. The service was, in fact, so persistent it was actually annoying at times. For instance, we would recieve a call on our voice mail after every time room service was delivered, or extra towels were delivered, or after we asked for an extra pillow. While we appreciate their concern, it gets old after a week, multiple times a day. There was only 1 bar in the whole hotel, other than in the restaurants. There were conventions there when we stayed and the bar/lobby area was packed and unusable. Very disappointing and annoying for such a HUGE hotel.The bathtub in our room was unable to modulate the hot and cold water (it would either be scalding or freezing, not in between). We had engineering in there 2 times, which upon the 2nd time, they offered us a new room. It was our last day so we declined, but there was cerainly no offer to reduce the bill. We are from the Phoenix area and there are a lot of other great places to stay that have much better ambiance and faciities. The service was great but it couldn't save the cold, institutional feel of this convention oriented hotel.

<Author>daisyhead21
<Content>Perfect For Christmas We took a family vacation to this resort for the Christmas holiday (2 parents  4 grown kids in our 20's). When we arrived we were warmly greeted by doormen  bellhops. The entrance was incredible  very welcoming. I am a self-described hotel snob and I was pleasantly surprised by how wonderful the resort was. The rooms were very clean  restocked with towels twice daily (morning  turn-down service). It was quite expansive, but just enough to feel like you had your own space. There were many little nooks where you could curl up with a book or take a nap in the sun  no one would know or care that you were there. The lobby had a nice bar  plenty of couches  tables to play card games on well into the night. There was live music every night - my only complaint is that they should have played later than 10 PM! I would recommend the Starbucks or Blue Sage Marketplace for breakfast. Although you are still going to pay $2 for a cookie, they are the only munchie place in the hotel. If you like healthy food eat at the Spa Bistro. It is open to everyone even if you don't use the spa. The food was very good  quite refreshing - - $9 for a healthy hamburger, not bad. We did eat at the Blue Sage restaurant for dinner  was not too happy with the service. All the other restaurants in the hotel were a bit out of our price range. I would recommend the Desert Ridge Marketplace across the street (nice walk, or catch the shuttle every 1/2 hour from the hotel). Although, it may look like a mall, there are not that many shops, but there are plenty of restaurants! We at at the Yard House. If you like beers, they have 84 on tap!!! They even put on our Packers for one of the football games!All in all, this would be my 1st pick of hotels if I was ever back in Phoenix. Contrary to some of the reviews on here (that had me a bit nervous before I went), this hotel is not business/conference centered. Yes, they have wonderful facilities for these events, but outside of that, it is all vacation  relaxation. If you go - have fun  check out the sunrises over the mountains - breath-taking!

<Author>RNY
<Content>Beautiful Setting We stayed at the Desert Ridge for one night in early December. It is a beautiful, well maintained resort. We weren't able to use the pools or tour the grounds because we were there during a two day heavy rain event (1.5 inches) - unusual for the desert setting. The resort is huge. The map that guests are given is one dimensional for a multi-dimensional facility. We've used maps to travel extensively but this map wasn't helpful. Even the desk clerk was confused by it and indicated the wrong wing for our room location. Since it was pouring outside we decided to use the fitness center but we never found it. The map didn't indicate how to access it and three staff members (two in suits and one in a uniform) that we asked didn't know either. One suited staff person finally told us how to get there but it was down a walkway outsde the hotel - in the pouring rain. It seemed really odd that there was no way to access the fitness center from inside the building. Adjacent to the resort is a Marriott time share facility which looks very nice. At the J.W. there are people trying to sell you a time share tour but they aren't pushy about it. The time shares have access to the J.W. restaurants and pools, although they have their own, so it could be a pleasant place to spend a week. We ate at the Tuscany Restaurant. The service and the food were excellent. The ambiance was very pleasant. It's an upscale restaurant geared toward adults. I wouldn't bring children to it. As usual at Marriott resorts, it was pricey but not outrageous and worth it for a special treat. Even with a few glitches the J.W. was a beautiful resort. If you want a big resort with lots of outdoor activities (and you think the weather will cooperate during your visit) this is a good choice.

<Author>Midnite13
<Content>Nice Hotel We stayed at the Marriott Desert Ridge in mid-November. Upon arrival, we checked in and were given a room on the 6th floor overlooking the botanical gardens, golf course and distant mountains. There was a small table and two chairs on the balcony. The room was clean and we had plenty of towels for our use. The shower stall tiles were a bit slippery and uneven. The beds were comfy and we had our choice of four pillows, two each of foam and feather.The ice machine was down the hall in an enclosed area and the free laundy (including detergent) was on the 4th floor.The only suggestion I would have is a screen for the sliding glass door. Coming from New England, I would have loved to keep the screen door closed and let the desert breeze in during the night.Staff in both the shops and restaurants were accommodating and gracious. The buffet breakfast is very expensive but there is a good variety. Lunch was busy but not a long wait - about 20 minutes. I put my name in coming back from the pool and went up to the room to change. When I came back, my table was waiting.Note there is a mall around the corner from this property and the hotel offers a free shuttle bus. There are restaurants, grocery store and a CVS there. Stock up on snacks and soda at these stores. We bought a case of water at CVS for the cost of a bottle at the Marriott.The grounds are beautiful and the lazy river was relaxing. I didn't have time to try the other pools but there were only a few people in one of the four other pools. The lobby area throughout the day and night was very busy and the the downstairs lobby bar area was very noisy in the evening. As mentioned in previous reviews, this hotel caters to a lot of meetings and conventions. However, every staff member greeted us with a smile. The concierge gave us great maps - better than Hertz. There is an onsite Hertz rental car service at the hotel which we used. Book ahead of time and be prepared to wait to get your car - it was about 30-40 minutes for us to get the keys for the vehicle.Would I stay there again - maybe. Nothing wrong with this hotel but I've stayed at other properties in Phoenix/Scottsdale which I felt had better amenities for about the same cost.

<Content>Beautiful I recently stayed at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge Resort  Spa Phoenix for a medical conference. Let me start by saying that this place is magnificent!! First of all, I never used the phone in the room. Secondly, I found out that the call  fee was placed after I had checked out and cleared my bill. I had to jump through a few hoops to prove my innocence (when it comes to hotel fees, you are guilty until proven innocent) and eventually get the charge removed. I believe that it was a honest mistake on Marriott鈥檚 part, however these post-check-out charges that show up on your credit card statement seems to be a recurring theme. So I would advise everyone that after having a fabulous time at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge Resort  Spa, check your bill and statement for a possible unexpected surprise.

<Author>Venturagal
<Content>SPA is A+...Hotel is C+ Ok. I am going to try to give some traveler some tips that will be helpful. We were flying in from out of state and needed an early check in. The hotel had agreed to this prior. We arrived at the hotel at 10 am (yes..i know...early). So, the room was not ready and we were fine with this. We checked our bag in and went to the pool. The pool was not anything great. The service was below average and we finally went to the bar to get our own drinks and food. AFter that, we never saw a waitperson again (or one that would actually do something). AFter flying and laying at the pool, i checked back in with the front desk at 1 (no room), 2 (no room), etc...finally my BF was mad and talked to the manager. Apparentely my boyfriend had booked a suite and the last peope had checked out late. We downgraded to a normal room just to check in. That kind of sucked for us looking for a much needed vacation.I found there to be tons of Marriott employees who walk around and smile and act helpful...but they are NOT helpful. It is like a bunch of robots walking around with fake shells. We ordered room service that night b/c we were exhausated and needed rest. The food came in a reasonable amount of time and the staff was fine. 20% gratutity was already added to our bill so we did not feel the need to tip her twice (i know we all have different opinions on this). The staff person left our room and CALLED us, asking why we had not tipped her?? Can you imagine?? We also did not receive housecleaning during our stay which i think is a nice hotel faux pas.Here is my big tip. Go to the adjacent spa. It is the best that i have ever been to. The staff are wonderful and the deep tissue massages are to die for (ask for susana). AFter the massage, you have access to the relaxing sauna, jacuzzi, etc and it is so relaxing. The spa has it's own pool away from the hotel that is A+. Very small, cushioned chairs, excellent food/beverage service,etc. Go the spa, get a treatment and stay there! Forever. Go to Spa pool and do not look back at the crummy Marriott pool. This hotel is designed for familes and for business travelers. There are conferences going on everywhere and there is no room for just the vacationer. It is a stressful feeling and everyone is walking around with conference badges. I was not impressed by anything but the spa. However, Roy's restaurant in the hotel is good and i would eat there again.I later learned that my BF was going to propose that trip but due to all of the problems has decided to wait for a better time. I hope that tells you all something.

<Author>feelnopain
<Content>Great, with one important exception... I stayed here for a professional and conference and generally enjoyed the experience. Rooms were nice, comfortable, with spacious bathrooms and I suspect there isn't a bad view in the place. Pool area was fantastic and not at all crowded. On site dining was excellent, although the lobby bar was absurdly overpriced. The conference facilities and food presentations were also excellent. The only issue was in service, particularly the disconnect between a remarkably responsive front desk and an apathetic housekeeping staff. The room got cleaned, but the attention to detail that you would expect at a resort of this calibe (or lower) was lacking. When I checked in, the clock on my nightstand was missing and one of the bedsheets was torn -- not anything to ruin the trip, but certainly annoying when you arrive late at night after a delayed flight and have to wait for the front desk to send up an alarm clock so you don't sleep through an early morning meeting. Throughout the stay, little details were always missed like removing the used towels but not replacing them or forgetting to empty the ice bucket. I admit that this are minor, but if you want to claim to be a five-star resort were guest can relax and unwind, they shouldn't have to deal with these annoyances.

<Author>Gus_Sanchez
<Content>Wonderful facility and overall experience! We have just returned from a week at the JW Desert Ridge Spa and Resort. The hotel is magnificent! The on-premises lazy river was on par with anything you'd find at a commercial water park (except much better - just a short walk from your hotel room).The service was really good. The only reason I hesitated in a 5-star rating is that we had a few housekeeping issues (conditioner vs. hand lotion). Unfortunately, the cleaning crew put a bottle of hand lotion in the shower and my wife used a glob of it on her hair! We had a few calls with management but they followed up and we resolved the issue amicably. Then, the next day, we had a few more, minor issues with towels, etc.. Again, we spoke with management and resolved the issue. - I'm not usually a nitpicker or complainer, but these little things, when added up, can be quite annoying. Anyway, that's the only reason I held off on the 5-stars. Otherwise, the staff was extremely friendly, pleasant and helpful. I used the Vacation Planner services, ahead of my stay, for booking a Grand Canyon tour with DeTours.Com. Which, by the way, was an awesome experience! Highly recommended! A bit more pricey (for a family of 4) than renting a car and going about it yourself, but, believe me, it's a bit of a haul, and you won't come anywhere close to the entertainment and learning value of going with an experienced guide. In our case, that was Bernie. He was great. We were also convinced to take the Maverick helicopter tour over/inside the canyon. That was an additional $232 per head and not an expense I had planned - but, again, highly recommended! - Anyway, the free vacation planning service offered by the resort was great! Use it!I also used the matching services of the Tennis Center, to find either other guests or local/community residents for a game. They found me a great partner from the community. Unfortunately, for me, I had to stop playing after the first set. The Pheonix sun was simply too much to be reckoned with (and this was at 8am)! Though I was keeping hydrated, I felt I was simply overheating. Didn't want to risk having to leave the resort in an ambulance ;-) I think evening play would have been a better choice (or at least doubles, where you don't have to work as hard).As you may have read in other posts, the food was kind of pricey. But, the phrase you get what you pay for does apply. The $12 Cobb salad could easily serve 3-4 people. The $10 Kokopelli Colada was extremely tasty and plentiful. I had breakfast at the Blue Sage restaurant on my first day and took advantage of the $21 buffet. Everything was absolutely delicious! Other days, we simply bought bagels or breakfast pasteries at either Starbucks (on premises) or the little counter outside Blue Sage. That wasn't so bad (pricey). I did not have dinner at any of the hotel restaurants, but, my friend (who was attending a trade show there) did have dinner at Roy's with a client. He absolutely LOVED his dinner there and highly recommends the restaurant.Finally, having read other readers' posts, I went ahead and booked a limo for our trip to/from the airport. As opposed to using SuperShuttle at $20/head ($80 in my case for a family of 4), I conducted an Internet search and chose First Class Executive Limo due to their (Barry's) quick and personal response. The experience was excellent! My kids were impressed with the driver holding up our name as we arrived at the airport (which, by the way, was about 90 minutes later than planned). The driver, Mary, was very friendly and patient. The car was a 2007 Town Car - spotlessly clean and absolutely beautiful! Barry kept all my charges on the credit card, including gratuity, and I didn't have to deal with having correct change, etc. It certainly was a first class experience at an almost 20% savings in cost!What can I say. This was, absolutely, the best facility in which I've stayed/vacationed. I don't normally like to vacation in the same spots (variety is the spice of life) but, believe you me, if I come back to the Phoenix/Scottsdale/Sedona area, I would absolutely return to the JW Desert Ridge! If anyone has any questions feel free to write me. Happy trails!

<Author>DCKathy
<Content>Fantastic beds, good food This is a fantastic hotel. Service was terrific. The beds are wonderful: very soft featherbeds that I could just sink into and not want to leave. The food at Roys was very good, especially the Disassembled Banana Pie dessert. It's a little far from downtown, but it's right next to a mall, which expands the food options to some more basic, less expensive places, like BJ's and an Asian Bistro. There's also a lovely wave pool with innertubes for floating. It's a very big place; so there's lots of walking to get from one side to another. I'd love to come back and see the spa and try that.My only complaint is that a hotel of this size should have more than two computers in the business center, which was run by FedEx Kinko's. At 40 cents a minute, surely they'd recover the cost in a month. While the gift shop is terrific, I think they can expand the business center a little into the gift shop and add a computer or two. It's very frustrating to have to wait to get on a computer when a big convention is going on.

<Content>Mixed Bag... We like to take 'local' trips every year, and we enjoy water parks. We normally stay at the Pointe South Mountain. This 24 hour line offered quick support on our needs - no room directory in the room, getting internet access, correcting some errors in our bill, issues with our pay per view TV. * Plenty of pool chairs with pitchers of ice water everywhereLows:* Pay per view movies didn't work. Engineer spent over 1 1/2 hours to try to fix the first night, but couldn't get it fixed until the next day.* Lazy river - closed the first day due to a storm. Once opened, it was nice, but not as nice as the Pointe. Mixed:* The room was 'ok'. Nothing special* The heavenly beds got mixed reviews. As my husband is big, my stepdaughter and I shared one bed, while he had the other. He said it was the best hotel bed he EVER slept in. We hated it! We both woke with stiff necks and backs. * A bit more pricey than some of the other local resortsWhile we had a good time, I'm not sure we would return. The water features were good, but not comparable to the Pointe South Mountain.

<Author>mel.w
<Content>A nice Marriott! We have recently stayed at this hotel- first time visitors to this particular Marriott -and found it most impressive. One thing that immediately struck - this is a LARGE hotel- much more so that suggested by websites etc. Whilst we were there - mid June - it was busy throughout, and seemed to have a mixture of business and leisure guests, although it was obvious that it is heavily used and promoted for business users. Rooms were very pleasant - all had balconies - and nicely decorated, if just a little lacking in table/ storage space -no drawers of any consequence, and one large table. A minor matter that caused no inconvienience tho. The bed was superb - extremely comfortable. Bathroom amenities/ turndown service/ housekeeping all of high standard. The pool areas, as discussed within this forum, are without doubt, the highlight of the property. No problems in finding lounger space- even tho the hotel was full. We only ate at tthe Blue Sage for breakfast, and had no complaints there. As seems to be common with a lot of Marriott properties, there is the usual time-share / condo sell, with representatives and desks evident - even messages left on the phone to come down and see us ! As stated - this is a large hotel, as a consequence, lots of car parking space required - be aware, it is a good 5-10 minute walk from parking the car to getting in the hotel, although there were some eager valets available should you wish.Overall- I was more than happy to have chosen Desert Ridge, with no substantial complaints at all.

<Author>purple_phantom
<Content>Sparkling property, but watch out for the hard sell! I just returned from four nights at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge. The hotel and rooms were beautiful. We had a room with 2 double beds, and while not huge, it was comfortably sized, and the bathroom is spacious and nicely appointed.The beds were very comfortable, and even with the soaring temperatures, the air conditioning worked well and was pretty quiet.This hotel has over 900 rooms, so you can imagine how large it is. We chose to self-park, not to save money but because I like the convenience of coming and going on a whim, being able to access things stored in the car, etc. The only problem with the free self-parking is that there are not adequate spaces, and you have to walk probably 1/4 to 1/2 a mile from the parking lots to the hotel. By the time you reach the lobby, you are practically suffering from heat exhaustion! Fortunately they have dispensers of cold water and iced tea in the lobby area.When we checked in, I was given a letter outlining the benefits of my Silver Elite membership. It's not a big deal to be in this category (only requires 10 nights per year or that you have a Marriott Visa card!) The letter said we could visit the Marriott Canyon Villas desk in the lobby to receive a deluxe postcard set. Of course, they want to sell you a membership in these timeshares. We also received a scratch-off lottery ticket upon check-in, that had to be scratched at the, guess where, Canyon Villas desk to see if you won some Marriott points.The icing on the cake was the recorded message we received on our last day, thanking us for staying with them. I thought what a nice touch until I kept listening to the message, which went on to offer us a great rate on a return visit ... of course you must book this through the Canyon Villas to see if you're eligible, etc! They just couldn't give up that last opportunity to try and sell something. Would definitely have been nicer if they had just thanked us for our patronage ... period!We didn't eat in any of the hotel restaurants, since there are so many wonderful choices in the Phoenix/Scottsdale area. It was great having a Starbucks on-site, but keep in mind that like most hotel-located Starbucks, they close around 8 p.m.All in all I would recommend the location because it was clean and beautiful, but just wanted to give a heads up about the parking situation and timeshare overkill.  
<Date>Jul 9, 2007

<Author>SDTraveler1
<Content>Review from a Convention Attendee I stayed here recently for a Convention (size: 600 people). Pay the $25 to valet park your car...the free parking lot is quite a hike in the heat. The hotel appears to be less than 5 years old, up to date, and well-appointed. The lobby is beautiful with water fountians that add much-needed moisture to the dry desert air. I loved the complimentary ice water and iced tea in the lobby - it was great after arriving from the heat outside. Check in was easy and the front desk staff were pleasant. All requests made via phone to the Marriott at Your Service desk were met promptly and accurately. (I requested additional face cloths and hangers). The Marriott at Your Service staff made follow-up calls to my room to ensure my requests had been adequately satisfied - a nice touch! My room had 2 beds because a King room was not available at the time I made my reservation. I moved to a King room for the last night of my stay. The King room is the same size as the double, but with more room to move around in due to there being one less bed. Both of my rooms faced out towards the Lazy River and pool, but the windows/walls were thick enough that I couldn't hear noise from those enjoying themselves outside. The bathroom was stocked with nice upgraded Artifact toilietries, not the usual Marriott items. The bathroom was pretty, but strange in that it had a small, glass-enclosed stand-up shower with separate bathtub. This was a meaningful detail to me because it is next to impossible to shave your legs in the shower...no place to put your foot up. The bathroom also had a strange absence of towel bars. My least favorite thing about the room was the fact that the carpet left my bare feet dirty, even though it looked clean. Yuck! The convention rooms were nice and it was fabulous to have a Starbucks on the property. I didn't get a chance to enjoy the Lazy River, but I heard lots of good things about it. My biggest complaint about this property was that it was very understaffed at a time when there were more than 3 conventions going on at the same time, especially in the evenings. For example, there was only one cocktail server working in the lobby lounge (at times there were more than 50 guests in the lounge) in the evenings and she nastily told everyone who arrived to get in line at the bar. The line at the bar was so long that it took a minimum of 25 minutes to get a drink. The hotel has a complimentary shuttle that runs every 30 minutes to the shopping center across the street. In the 110+ degree heat, we were glad we didn't have to walk over. I ate lunch at the Blue Sage (very good chicken quesadilla prepared the traditional way our server suggested, not the strange inside-out way described on the menu). We also had brunch at the Blue Sage on Sunday. The brunch buffet was a zoo, so we ordered off the menu. When our items took more than a 20 minutes to arrive, our server suggested that we get some fruit from the buffet to enjoy until our entrees arrived. This hotel has the potential to be a 4 star hotel, if they improve the consistency of their service.

<Author>LaCoop
<Content>Beautiful Property Caters to Conventions/Special Events We shared this Spring Vacation with another couple, both having experienced the JW Marriott Camelback Inn and Renesaience in Scottsdale in the past 2 years. After reviewing this property online, and knowing Marriott's trademark of exceptional service we were looking forward to our 5 day stay at this fairly new property. Both couples stayed in Standard King rooms at $549 per night.Upon Thursday afternoon check in, our room was on the 3rd floor, directly above the main driveway/valet enterence. With this rate, the noise and traffic which included 3 buses were a surprise. The bellboy was assuring us these were the last bus arrivals for the day. As he spoke, 2 more could be seen approaching. Our request for another room was not immediately remedied, but an hour later we were told we could move, but we would be very far from each other. We still agreed after realizing the distance was most extreme! There are 950 rooms here so we were off to Egypt on our own, no offer of assistance. We laughed this off as glad to have the opportunity to be removed from the driveway noise and fumes. Later we met our friends in the huge and most beautiful lobby and waited forever on the patio to be acknowledged and served drinks. We decided to move inside and found a spot near the bar so our husbands could serve us rather than die on the vine. The people watching was fabulous tho- Obviously lots going on. A reception was queing up before entering their poolside designation. We noticed an entire outdoor common area had been roped off- and this was the beginning of how things were going to go - removing pool areas, lawn areas, patio areas for convention meals, receptions, MLB club members and special events. The vacationer's space got smaller and smaller as the weekend proceeded. All the pool's furniture filled up in the early morning either with bodies or saved with books and towels. Poolside service was very stressed, and there were long waits to order- and to receive orders. We watched as other guests lost patience and learned that the management had no time for regular duties as they followed up with personal apologies. I have no idea why they were so short-staffed, as the complex is designed to serve the masses. Perhaps that is the downfall, as the staff did not seem to enjoy or handle their positions under stress and there is no excuse for runnng it understaffed. We dined at Tuscany, it was fabulous and here the staff knew how to treat and please their guests and allowed us to feel like we were in Europe where it is impolite to hurry the guest along or present an unrequested check. This was our favorite meal of the entire trip! Roy's was a great environment, on patio outside. The food was also good but you will have to pay to get any amount of it, salads and accompaniments are separate. Their location is more visual to the hotel masses and here we knew that our table was scheduled for another reservation behind us. Reservations are a must, suggest later dining to avoid being rushed.The onsite Starbuck's had huge lines all mornings and usually ran out of breakfast items and popular ingredients before we got up. The hotel was full the entire time we were there, not just the weekend.We went to the spa on 2 different days: peds and manis on one visit, maggages the other. Never have we paid more for salon services, but were happy to have the use of the spa included which isn't always the norm for pedi/mani services. The massages were excellent but construction was underway next to the pool, tractors and alot of dirt and dust aloft along with the noise. There are many spas in the Phoenix area and this one dosen't come close to the atmosphere or relaxation available at JW Marriott's Camelback Inn - there is where you will find spa bliss! Our husbands golfed on site - very expensive for the quality - they are used to the Trune courses in Arizona and there is no comparrison except in fees.We were certainly paying enough and know what the resort experience should be. After a few days of not being treated as JW Marriott guest's reputation holds, we managed to get rooms in JW's nearby real resort Camelback Inn. This property is much older and smaller - but if you are expecting service and an relaxing atmosphere you will be treated as the most important guest that you deserve to be and would expect when staying at a resort. The Desert Ridge is a Convention Complex. All the amenities are a huge bonus and a great addition to the convention experience, resulting in positive reviews from the business traveler, and a huge dissappointment to the vacationeer!I shouldn't close without mentioning the middle of the night fire drill. The continued blaring sirens emptied bathrobed guests into hallways. I felt horrible for the parents of wailing children but the worst of it was that there was no communication. Remember, our rooms were at the farthest point, Egypt, and it was a hike with and without use of elevators towards the lobby. Since this turned out to be a false alarm it was unfortunate that staff did not send runners or use the PA system to explain the situation. They did record and deliver a phone message hours later that blamed the incident on a guest, suggesting that he was drunk in the bar and pulled down on an alarm. I don't like to quote over used phrases, but when we left the Desert Ridge I said to my friend, Been here, Done that, Won't be back.

<Author>Togtog
<Content>Great, Relaxing Stay at the JW Marriott Overall, we had a great stay at the JW Marriott Resort in Desert Ridge. Since our stay was over Memorial Day weekend, we thought we would have some hassle checking in, etc. However, it was smooth and quick and the woman who checked us in was very pleasant.The room was wonderful with a beautiful view of the pool, golf course and desert landscape. The bathroom was a good size with a separte walk-in shower and bathtub. The service we appreciated was the nightly turn-down service which also included refreshing the towels if needed. We travel quite a bit and unfortunately have encountered nice resort hotels which have the worst sound-proofing . . . however, we slept through the night without having to endure any outside noise. Having kids, this is a plus.The pool was great and is where we spent most of our time. Being 100 plus degrees outside there were plenty of umbrellas (we had no problem finding chairs w/ an umbrella in the morning, however, it did get crowded by late morning). Also, there were staff members handing out pitchers of ice water and popsicles throughout the day. The food you can order at the pool was good and the service was quick. There is also a great kid's menu (we were not given the kid's menu and had to request it).There were a lot of activities at the hotel during our stay including a movie shown by the pool every night, a cowboy camp night with s'mores and a native american family who performed traditional dances.The fitness center could be a little bigger. If you want to go on the treadmill or do weight machines it's not a problem. If you do mat work or free weights, first of all there are no mats and secondly there is very limited space to work out.The Desert Ridge Marketplace nearby has something for everyone. There are several restaurants including California Pizza Kitchen, Rock Bottom Brewery, the Yardhouse and Macaroni Grill. Great restaurants for kids. There is also a movie theater and the outdoor mall had a lot of your typical mall stores. We will definitely return to this hotel!

<Content>Superb stay at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge Just got back from a great Memorial weekend getaway. On every level this hotel scored an A in my opinion. I was immediately impressed by the quick check in and friendly staff. For instance upon entering my room I noticed a problem with the a/c. For example at the pool, employees handed out pitchers of ice water, iced towels, freeze pops, etc, etc. Hmmm, I didn't receive any ot these things on a recent stay at the Ritz Carlton in Maui! The concierge was knowledgeable, accessible and very accommodating. The rooms were always spotless and tended to multiple times per day. The bathrooms were what you would expect a 4plus star hotel to have.The balcony was clean and spacious enough to stretch out a bit. The ability to print your boarding pass in the lobby....huge plus. Starbucks on site need I say more? The golf courses although a little brown from the weather still top notch. If I were to have one complaint it would be the lack of an adult only pool. There are 5 pools on site and all of them were filled with screaming kids. Unless you're by one of the fountains you won't receive a lot of quiet time. Overall a fabulous experience...
