<Author>CNorm
<Content>Beautiful resort My husband and I were at this beautiful resort for 2, all too short days, for a conference he attended May 9 - 11. While my husband attended meetings I floated in a tube in the lazy river pool (and I was certainly not the only adult in the lazy river pool). This property is absolutely stunning, gorgeous grounds, tastefully decorated rooms and a bathroom I wish I had in my own home (marble, granite and travertine). The beds were comfy, though I would have preferred firmer pillows.Neither my husband nor I found the hotel staff to be snotty or rude as another reviewer mentioned. Everyone we encountered was helpful and friendly. The concierge even gave us a much better suggestion for transportation back to the airport (and made the reservation for us as well) than what we were originally planning to do.We took SuperShuttle from PHX to the hotel for $19 p/p. A little time was wasted in making various stops within the airport to pick up more passengers and then having to stop at another hotel to drop someone off, but this is the nature of SuperShuttle. However, the driver was quite competent. But for our return to the airport we took TransStyle Limousine for $22 p/p. It's a town car that takes just 4 people. We were at the airport in 20 minutes.One other convenient (and free) perk was that you could print out your airline boarding passes at a computer in the lobby near the front desk. The computer only prints boarding passes, but for about 20 airlines. We appreciated this convenience.Food at the hotel: the restaurants are pricey, as one would expect them to be at an upscale property. My husband brought me breakfast from the spread at his meeting, but I did have lunch at the pool one day. I thought the prices were reasonable ($12 for a very large and filling spinach salad and $5 for a smoothie). I had seen other people's orders and knew, before I ordered my lunch, that the portions were plentiful.For dinner we took the complimentary shuttle to the Desert Ridge shopping/dining/entertainment complex across the street from the property (the property is large and also encompasses the Marriott Vacation Club, so the shuttle is necessary). There were many good dining choices with many price ranges at Desert Ridge.My only disappointment was some of the equipment in the fitness center. My husband and I are both gym rats, and we both love the elliptical trainer. Some are better than others and the ones at this Marriott were not good at all. Very awkward and uncomfortable to use, so ended up running on the treadmills (which were quite good and had personal TV's with complimentary earphones).Though we were here for a short conference, I would definitely consider returning for a long weekend sometime, perhaps even a sisters/girlfriends trip. It's perfect for that.

<Content>Girlfriend getaway weekend Just returned from 4 days at this property and after reading the rest of the reviews both before and after I went, they are all pretty true on what is good/bad. 6 mos. ago we stayed at the JW on Capri, Italy and it was head and shoulders above this JW in Scottsdale. Scrub and wrap combo was a good bang for the buck but massage seemed to be given by a newbie....Same with Roy's- I have eaten at 2 diff. Roy's locations and this staff was not up to par at all...food was excellent as always though. It seemed much of staff might have been college students on break for the summer or ?? While we were expecting it to be HOT in May, it was 102....pitchers of ice water by the pool and lobby were nice ...cement and stone by the pool scorching your bare feet- not nice.Pluses of the property is that the food at ALL of the restaurants on site was wonderful-we tried them all. Room service, too. Mini bar prices were actually fairly reasonable for a property like this. <Author>want2getaway
<Content>Loved the JW Marriott We loved our 3 day stay at the this Resort. It is a lovely property, very large and spread out. The rooms were large, very clean and the bathroom was well appointed. No problems with the service but nothing outstanding to report either. We had room service for breakfast each morning. The breakfasts were wonderful in taste and presentation and service was good. Lunches at the restaurant on site as well as the cafe in the spa were both enjoyable. We both had massages at the spa and they were very nice. Since this is such a large property we liked that we had many choices of seating during the day. One day we enjoyed the afternoon by the smaller pool area behind the spa, very quiet and adult oriented, another day we sat poolside by the main pool, very busy but nice and another day we sat reading by the restaurant outside the lobby area. The lazy river would be enjoyed by my kids if we return to this property. The only down side would be if you are looking for personal service, this is such a large resort and property that it loses that personal touch of other 5 star resorts like a Ritz Carlton or Four Seasons. We did not leave the resort but understood from others that it is a drive to get anywhere. Overall, I would recommend this resort.

<Author>Rouget
<Content>Can't Handle the Crowds April 8, 2007. My family just returned from spending Spring Break at the Marriott Desert Ridge. It is a pretty property, although surrounded by ugly construction. Our rooms were fine, quiet but overlooked the ugly construction. Problems arose on our first evening when we tried to dine at one of the resort's several restaurants. We had difficulty getting a reservation and then had to suffer long waits for service at Roy's. The next morning at breakfast, there was a large line of people waiting for a table and a long wait for service. Lunch by the pool? We waited over an hour for four sandwiches! Next morning for breakfast, the line and wait were longer (over half an hour, we were told) so we decided to try to snag breakfast at the Starbucks on the property. By 9:15 a.m., Starbucks was out of food except giant MM cookies! We ended up getting in the car and heading to a nearby mall for bagels. We were told that the hotel was only 50% booked, yet they seemed incapable of feeding the number of people that were staying there.Other problems: crowds at the pools meant no available pool chairs for anyone arriving after 9 a.m. - yet the resort allowed people to reserve chairs in choice locations with towels. We had to scrounge for two chairs and then lift and move them ourselves. Meanwhile, someone had placed towels and newspapers on 7 chairs in a nice, shady location and did not show up to sit in them for several hours. When someone complained to a pool attendant, nothing was done. I would not return to this resort - next year, I'll try the Phoenician.

<Author>cinder1997
<Content>Marvelous Marriot This hotel/resort is all luxury. The grounds and public areas of this resort are beautiful. The hotel offers a daily list of activites that the you can take part in some being free of charge and some at a small fee. For example they offered a desert walk with a desert plant expert. Across from the resort is a very nice complex of stores and resautarants to enjoy for those of you not wanting to eat or spend all of your time at the resort. The rooms are nicely decorated, but the bathrooms are gorgeous. Bathrooms offer a seperate shower and bath area, all marble tile, and our huge in size. Each room has a balcony and in room cofffee or tea. Parking is either valet or free self park. The pool area is exceptional and offers a lazy river area. There were many families with children staying at this resort. All in all this is a beautiful and comfortable place to stay with out being too stuck up. We loved it!

<Author>mevangelista
<Content>Top Shelf This hotel's accomodations and ameniteis were awesome, as was the service, scenery and most of the food. The staff had it all working. Customer service at its best. Played both courses, all good. Friends ate at the steakhouse on property and said it ws excellent. Also ate at the Italian restaurant on property and it was OK and expensive. Breakfast buffett is expansive and expensive. Be prepared to have money fly out of your wallet for everything, but this is a high end, luxary resort in the desert and that is to be expected. The resort is big, 400 plus rooms so know that before you go. Also, it is located way out in n/e Phoenix on the border of north Scottsdale. Everything in this area is spread out. If you don't have a rental car, be prepared for a car service or taxi ride to Old Town Scottsdale costing between 50 and 60 dollars one way, plus tip. There are great bars and restaurants between the resort and downtown Scottsdale. Both Devil's Martini Bars were great. Dos Gringos was casual and fun and for a high end steakhouse (really high end), but absolutely fabulous for the food, decor and bar and people scene, try Drinkwater's City Hall Steakhouse in Old Town. From there you can walk to just about all the other bars and nighclubs. It was all good. Personally, I would have liked my resort to be about half the size of this one and half the distance to Old Town Scottsdale, but I was part of a golf group and it was not my call. But this place is all good, with great service. Definately 5 stars.

<Author>thedcdiva
<Content>Lovely Property with Great Service We have just returned from a weekend at the Desert Ridge. The hotel is magnificent and the service matched it. Although we do not play golf, we found plenty to do on the vast property. Although it is extremely large, it was not hard to find a peaceful spot.  We stayed in a standard room overlooking the main pool and patio. There was constant activity on the patio, but it was never noisy or bothersome. The rooms were spacious, well appointed and just plain pretty. All have a balcony, and a bath with a seperate tub and shower. The pool is really a pool complex, with several different pools and hot tub. Although the hotel was fully booked, the pool never really seemed crowded. The Spa is enourmous and seemed extremely busy, but that did not take away from the experience in any way. The treatments, were expensive but wonderfully relaxing. The restaurants we tried were quite good. We ate most often at Blue Sage, which had a great breakfast menu including a impressive looking buffet that we did not get around to trying. We also tried the Meritage Steak house which offered wonderful food and ambiance, but at a steep price. But for dinner, we usually ventured out to nearby Scottsdale. Overall, a wonderful spot and I would definitely return.

<Author>md814
<Content>Very nice resort - great golf course We stayed at this resort for a company function and were very pleased. The bathrooms were large, very clean, and had plenty of counter space. We had a great sized walk in shower and separate bathub with dual sinks.The room was well spaced and had a nice view and balcony. It's nice to have a Starbucks and some other good little stores directly in the the resort. The staff was very polite, friendly and hospitable. Room service was very good. Massage was fantastic. Also, loved the convenience of the Desert Ridge Marketplace directly across the street. Try Grill Expeditions restaurant - awesome food! The Marketplace offers many restaurant choices and shopping. The resort offers 2 wonderful golf courses, and if you just want to work on your game, pay the $20 a day for unlimited range balls. My husband spent hours there not only on the driving range, but practicing his short game, as they putting greens plus sand traps and short game practice facilities.All in all, a very nice, upscale resort. Perfect for the golf/spa vacation or just to have a beautiful resort to stay in with access within minute to great shopping and restaurants. TIP: Go to the front desk and directly across from it, print your boarding pass to avoid the lines at the airport. It's a free service Marriott offers. Check in at night to avoid lines - you can do so up to 24 hrs before your flight.

<Author>SFO2004
<Content>Great hotel and great service I recently stayed at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge for a conference. I was there for 3 nights. The hotel is very nice! The common areas were nicely decorated and there were plenty of seating areas.The rooms were well appointed. The beds are very comfortable and the bathrooms were a great size, with separate tubs and marble shower stalls. I only wish the tub was a soaking tub! There was also a nice balcony with a table and chairs, overlooking the putting green and some outside seating.One of the best things about this hotel is the service! Everyone was very professional and very courteous. Even under the pressure of serving that many people (over 1000) lunch at the same time, the service staff always came through with a smile. The shuttle to the mall across the street was very helpful. The only problem I had with service was with a young girl at the front desk. She didn't seem to know what she was doing and wasn't very courteous.The other cons are that the hotel is huge and caters to conferences. Since that is what I was here for, it didn't bother me. But, I did notice vacationers trying to get through the crowds, and I don't think I would like that if I were on vacation.Overall, I would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>PennStater84
<Content>Marriott Desert Ridge/Phoenix trip I recently attended a conference at this resort (which I understand was sold the week after we left!) and was very impressed with the service, staff, and appearance. This hotel isn't near downtown so be aware there's nothing in walking distance that I could see. It was also about a 20 minute and $55 taxi ride from the airport. It was unseasonably cold during our stay (wouldn't you know - we were trying to escape the cold!) so even though the pools and lazy river were heated, they were closed because of the temps. They appeared to be well-maintained and the landscaping with markers naming the plants and trees was just beautiful.The front desk staff and all hotel staff we encountered were very pleasant and helpful. The concierge staff even created driving directions for us from point A to point B to point C and back to the hotel when we told them our tourist-y plan for my 1 free day!! We rented a car from the on-site Hertz place.We enjoyed the Frank Lloyd Wright camp tour, (Talieson West), old towne Scottsdale and Rawhide - the re-created old West town complete with fake shoot-outs. Hokey- yes, a little, but great fun and great photo opps! Looked like a movie scene.My husband and teen daughter had a great time on the Detours guided van tour to the Grand Canyon which also stopped at Sedona and a reservation and included lunch for $130. The concierge encouraged that tour group because of the cushier seats for the long drive up and back (4.5 hrs each way). There wer others that were cheaper, but I'm glad we booked this one - they got a great guide. My daughter was spouting off facts and info about plants, geology, etc for days afterwards.The hotel's free shuttle to the nearby Desert Ridge Marketplace ran every half hour or less and was very handy, since otherwise you'd need a car to get anywhere. (or go broke on taxis to get downtown) We ate most of our meals over there, since they had California Pizza Kitchen, TGI Fridays and other non-chain but similar places and the restaurants at the hotel looked expensive for our tastes.The hotel also provides internet service (not wireless in the rooms though) plus free local and long distance calls for 9.95 plus taxes a day. We enjoyed the live musicians each night in the lower lobby/bar area - very classy to a teenager and even her mom!

<Author>kls_katidid
<Content>Great Service, Okay Resort My husband and I stayed at this resort for 3 nights, Oct 8-10. The staff at this place were really great. Very kind and attentive and willing to do whatever it took to make our stay enjoyable. There was a woman who was checking in when we were checking in and it turned out she was at the wrong JW in Phoenix, so the front desk attendant arranged to have one of the resort's town cars take her to the correct hotel so she didn't have to pay for yet another taxi. That's what I call great service!We picked this hotel for three reasons: 1 - lazy river/pool complex; 2 - spa (for me); 3 - golf (for hubby). If we were attending a conference, I might have given this resort a higher rating, but as a leisure hotel, it is only okay (especially given the high price). 1. The lazy river/pool was great, but a little on the cool side and always dirty with bugs and debris swirling right around the loop with you. Pool bar/cafe food was what I've come to expect from pool bar food - expensive and mediocre.2. The spa environment was wonderful. The facilities were beautiful, peaceful and serene and the staff was okay. The massage I received was probably the worst I've ever had, and at $150 for 50 minutes, I was hugely disappointed. 3. I'm not a golfer, but my husband was pretty disappointed with the course he played (there are two and one was closed - unfortnately I can't remember which one he played). I guess it's the wrong time of year for golf in PHX, but still, for the price he expected a lot better. Our room was nice; bedding was heavenly. Shower pressure was terrible and so I called the front desk. Within an hour, maintenance had come, removed the old shower head, located and installed a new one and the pressure was much better. There was a cockroach in our room the first morning, but it was clearly on its last leg and was the only bug of any kind we encountered in our ground floor room. We didn't eat any meals at the resort (except lunch at pool bar). There is a great mall right across the street with tons of restaurants.

<Author>dje
<Content>Disappointed. Stayed at this resort for 2 days in August. Coincidentally before our stay, USA Today published an article about how great the pool area was. Perhaps this set expectations too high, as this resort was a huge disappointment.On the plus side, the grounds and overall property and design were very nice. Rooms has a garden, floral design and bathroom was huge with a nice shower. There is a nice computer system for rent in each room, and you could use it to efficiently make requests to the front desk or housekeeping (this part of the system was free). Property is also located next to Desert Ridge mall where you can find a bunch of shopping, restaurants, Target, etc.However, the resort experience left alot to be desired. The key item, as mentioned in other posts, is a faulty air conditioning system. The hallways smelled damp and musky. While the room A/C was better, it never cooled sufficiently or removed the humidity levels. Further, the pool area was awful. This could have been a result of this weekend being the most busy in the season (heard through another guest as claimed by their staff), but there were no seats, used food plates everywhere. It didn't quite live up to their Top 10 billing in USA Today.Hoping these guys will clean up their act and make this worth of the J.W. Marriott brand.

<Author>amzamz
<Content>This hotel keeps me coming back Stayed for a long weekend over Labor Day. YES - it was crowded but it was a holiday weekend. With that in mind, the crowds were tolerable.When I pulled up to the valet, I was asked what they could for me. When I said I wanted to drop off my bag and then park the car, I was a bit disappointed to be told to pull my car over and take the bag inside myself. Sure they were busy, but it was 104 outside and I hadn't intended to handle the bag myself.This was a repeat trip and I decided to try the Cloub Club. Not sure that it is worth the extra money though. The Cloub Club employees were exremely hospitable and went out of their way to ensure you had a fresh drink or were partaking of the breakfast, appetizers, etc. But really can a person consume $150 worth of food and drinks per day!! You do get a small gift upon arrival and a packet of stationary at departure. I spent my days at the Revive Spa which never felt crowded. I am a spa junkie and must say that Winnie gave me the VERY BEST hot stone massage. When my 80 minutes were up, I wanted to beg her to start all over! Cheryl also does a excellent facial. I noted their names and will request both of them on my next visit. If you like either of those services, you will not be disappointed.Dinner at Roy's was superb - very attentive service too. I like breakfast at Blue Sage - other meals there are OK - not great but not overpriced considering that you are in a hotel. Overall this hotel keeps me coming back - very comfortable rooms, 99% ot their employees are outstanding. Why stay anywhere else?

<Author>wahooaz
<Content>Overall a great experience, but some issues... We stayed for Labor Day weekend. Overall we had a great time, but there were some issues.We had a nice room... the beds were very comfortable, the bathroom was nice and had a separate shower, and there was a balcony with a small table and two chairs. However, although it was a step above the average room, it wasn't a very large or luxurious. The room service was reasonably priced and delivered quickly, which we liked, and had a kids menu for $6.50. The spa was incredible... my husband and I each had a massage there, and stayed for a few hours to lounge by the blissfully quiet, uncrowded spa pool and use the other services such as the steambath, jacuzzi, etc.The first issue was that the hallways were really hot and muggy. It seemed like they didn't air condition the hallways. It was a bit of a walk to get to our room, and by the time you got there you were sweaty and uncomfortable.The second issue is that they charged $20 a night for valet overnight parking. I can see that in a city, but we are talking the middle of the desert here. When we drove up to the main entrance, they asked us if we wanted to valet, and we said yes, and if we would be parking overnight, and we said yes (since we wouldn't be leaving the resort), but they didn't mention the $20 charge (until we saw it on the bill, LOL!)The third issue has to do with the pools. They advertise the pools as their big attraction during the summer. And while they were nice, they were REALLY crowded. All the chairs were taken (or at least they seemed to be taken, since there were towels on them), but no one seemed to actually be using them. If you asked a server how to get a chair, they said to get there early and put a towel on it, doh! We ended up just leaving our beach bag and clothes next to a bush every day we were there.Then, in order to get into the pool, you don't just need a key card, you need a one of those plastic bracelets that you clip on and it won't come off unless you cut it. I understand that it is to keep out non-guests, but they are uncomfortable if you have to wear them for 3 days (especially our 3 year old, who kept pulling on it). We cut ours off overnight, and when we asked for new ones at the front desk the next morning, they gave us a hard time about it. When we put them on the next time, we put them on ourselves so they were loose and we could pull them off. Don't let the front desk people put them on for you... they put them on REALLY tight.Then, if you want a pool towel, you have to give your room number (shouldn't the little bracelet be enough?). Its not like you can steal the towels, since there is a guard at the pool gate who makes you take them off from around your waist as you leave and put them in a hamper (not that we were trying to steal them, but our 3 year old was shivering and we wanted to just carry him to the room wrapped in the towel... and just leave the towel there for the housekeeping staff.) I was really worried the rest of the trip that they would charge me for the pool towels, since I checked them out one place with my room number, and returned them to the hamper on the way out.Then there is the lazy river, which is a ton of fun, IF you can get a tube. There is a limited number of tubes floating in the river, and you have to wait for one to become vacant to get one (the only thing you don't have to prove you are a guest to do, LOL!). However, people were hogging them, taking them back to their towel-draped chairs, using two to float instead of just one. It took about a half hour to find a tube for our 7 year old daughter to use to float. The kids also enjoyed the water slide, where they thankfully had a guard at the water slide line, so that there wasn't cutting/pushing/shoving.Also, the service at the pool left a lot to be desired. If you want service, you need to be at a chair and put up your flag, but there aren't enough chairs for the all the guests. My husband kept trying to wave down servers, then finally gave up and went to the restaurant and got us some drinks (not that it was a huge hardship, but it would be nice to be able to get cold drinks when it is over 100 degrees outside).Lastly, at one point they ran out of towels for about 30 minutes. You have to go to this centrally located ramada to get pool towels. On our last day I went with my daughter, soaking wet, to get some towels. They had run out. The attendant kept saying towels were coming, but they never came. At one point an official looking person came by to make sure the attendant REALLY meant there were no towels, and checked all the empty towel shelves to make sure they were REALLY empty, and then disappeared. After a long wait, we just gave up and walked back to our room wet.I think we would have enjoyed our stay more if it wasn't a holiday (Labor Day) and it wasn't so crowded, but the management should be able to anticipate when the hotel is full and plan accordingly (enough towels, enough servers, etc.) Also, they need to put some kind of system in place to ensure that people don't hog chairs and tubes.

<Author>michelescully
<Content>Still love the Desert Ridge This was my third stay at this hotel. We had a most enjoyable time here last year and I was hopeful that it would prove to be as good this year. I was travelling with my twelve year old son so requested a room with a computer (rather than travel with a laptop) and this was granted with an upgrade to a room with a great view over the pools and mountains. The rooms are a reasonable size - with two queen beds, a spacious bathroom with shower and a balcony. We ate breakfast in the Blue Sage most days - buffet with my son paying around $9 and mine being $19.50 - a relaxing way to start the day - especially when suffering from jet lag and waking very early in the morning during our first few days in arizona. We spent some time by the pool most days and these were rarely crowded - but were noisier at the weekends when large groups of 'young (ish) men and women' would drink (a fair amount) and generally get quite loud as they turned pink in the arizona sunshine - golf parties or conference attendees - i don't know. There were many 'local' families on one occasion being allowed into the pool area by residents - you need a room key to access the pool area, they just asked if they would open the gates for them! It didn't seem to be a big problem really as the hotel pools are large and this is the off season.We ate pool side on several occasions and the food was fine - although one server over charged us on several occasions (the hotel put this right when I checked out). We had one meal (on our last day - and the server then told us that on purchasing one drink from the pool area (soft) we were entitled to refills all day (news to us) - I wonder if that will be the case next summer? - although we'd never been told this before.We ate room service often - my son prefers it, and it was usually pretty promptly delivered and generally warm. There is a 20% charge + $3 and tax added to each order - ouch! We were able to order using the inroom computer and confirm availability online - so my son was able to order the food for us this year - a nice touch.Check in and out of the hotel were easy and my special requests were met (computer and fridge). Most of the staff are attentive and helpful - always polite and friendly - the pool staff less so this year than last.We made use of the complimentary laundry service - with soap and softener provided - and left with clean clothes to finish our arizona holiday in the marriott canyon villas.We will be back here next year - we love the location, scenery and the service you get in the off-season. And as Brits we LOVE the sun......

<Author>VaBelle35
<Content>There are great things about this place and not so great things I have mixed feelings about this hotel. I was traveling for business as a single woman, but with a group of people from work and a family member. My company paid for everything during my stay. The room was large, clean and the bed was incredibly comfortable. I was not overwhelmed by the spa or salon and they don't have their act together coordinating services between them. The massage I had was just okay, nothing to sing about. The food provided for the convention was usually dry and not exciting, but that may have more to do with the choices made by the organizers than the hotel. I could not get my room cold no matter how low I turned the thermostat. It sat on 62 the entire time and I still was too hot to blow dry my hair. As some reveiws have stated, the hallways are hot and muggy. On some days some hallways were and on other days none of them were. The FedEx office had no a/c on my last day there and it was unbearable in there. I highly recommend using their Sony Picture Developer as I developed my digital photos and the Sony machine really does a fantastic job. The service at the hotel is outstanding, I was always satisfied with how they handled problems (several small things like the made threw out my newspaper before I had read it and I need a box to ship things home). The hotel did not coordinate my car to the airport, but I was still able to get one. They say to reserve it 24 hours in advance but also re-confirm it a couple of hours before (says my driver). I never did go outside, too oppressively hot. I have to agree with the restaurant recommendations, thumbs up to Blue Sage (my #1 choice) and Roys and thumbs down to the steakhouse. I never had the time to try the Italian place as it is closed 2 nights a week.

<Author>PHX_Travel
<Content>Muggy rooms in the summertime My husband had a lengthy conference at the JW Marriot Desert Ridge the end of July. While the lobby and grounds were beautiful, the hotel has major problems with its air conditioning. We were assigned a beautiful suite overlooking the pool, and we could not get the room temperature below 83 degrees. The hotel's engineering department admitted that the rooms at the end of the halls are also at the end of their cooling loop and do not get adequate cooling. In addition, our lovely bathroom that was big enough to have a dance floor in it, had no vents or air conditioning supply. It was unbearable. We literally kept the door open with fans blowing the slightly cooler air from the hallway (which was still very warm) into the room. The hotel moved us to another room in the area....but same problem. We finally gave up our suite and moved to a standard room closer to the lobby and the air conditioning was at best, adequate (we kept our fan!). MANY of the conference rooms were too hot, and other rooms seemed to be cool then hot, as if the hotel was moving its inadequate cooling capabilities around. The pool areas are nice, and service was ok...beyond the seemingly unfixable air conditioning problem.If you're thinking of booking a conference/meeting at this property in the summer, my advice is don't do it. If you're just wanting to take the family for a night or two, ask for a centrally located room and it will probably be ok.

<Author>BaronVonH
<Content>A Marriott on steroids We stayed at the hotel because of a business conference, not so much by choice, and I think we would have chosen elsewhere, if not for the business conference. The rate was quite high for the off-season, considering the level of service and the quality of the room. Maybe if I was a golfer I would have been more excited, but this resort is out on the edge of town, a 20-30 minute drive from the nightlife of Scottsdale. The hotel is big, and I think that may be part of the problem. It's very dificult to provide top service to over a thousand guests. House cleaning was quite slow and the halls seemed to be filled with maids carts all the time. We had numerous problems getting internet connections (should be better at a nearly new hotel), and the staff weren't much help. Wireless and high-speed in the room were two separate charges, for each computer. In fairness, the hotel did remove most of our Internet charges.There are several food options, quite acceptable and reasonably priced, given that this is an expensive resort. The pools are very nice, and they are generously staffed with attendants. The pool area seemed to be the most service-oriented part of the hotel. Many other folks were going through the motions or a little rough around the edges. This is not a Ritz-Carlton.This a very nice property, and families will enjoy a trip to this resort more than a trip to Las Vegas. But the place didn't feel that special, and I think I would have preferred to stay at one of the more established resorts closer in to the center of Scottsdale (most of which are the same price or less expensive.)

<Content>Not impressed... My husband and I just returned from a weekend getaway at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge. We鈥檙e Phoenix residents, but like to check out the local hotels and spas. This was our first visit to this property. We have stayed at other JW Marriott properties and were impressed. Not so with this property. The lobby and grounds are beautiful. The wet areas are minimal, and overall, the spa accommodations are only so-so. We did enjoy the spa pool, which is much less crowded than the other pools at the resort. It was quiet and relaxing, with the exception of an inconsiderate guest yapping continuously on her cell phone. The Spa Bistro served tasty food with efficient, courteous service. We dined at Roy鈥檚, where the service was exceptional and the food on par with other Roy鈥檚 locations. I will return to this Roy's location. However, I will not stay at this property again. Given a choice, I would book the Camelback Inn, which has a sumptuous spa and guest accommodations that offer what I expect from a JW Marriott.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Ignore the hype - especially on July 4th Weekend Reading all of the reviews on this site, my wife and I decided to stay at the JW Marriott over the 4th July period, and I have to say the hype does not match the resort. OK, a nice, lavish, well decorated hotel it is, but there are many negatives. The Lazy River was not so much lazy as manic, and there were countless people smoking on rafts and drinking from brought in cans of beer - more like the Salt River than the lazy River. The hotel clearly does not splash out on air conditioning the common areas, a clear issue when it is 110 degrees. The drinks are overpriced, and the service was average - definitely nothing to amaze. I have travelled extensively throughout the world, and have never seen a valet service staffed entirely by 17 and 18 year old kids, nor been refused access to walk around the pool area as I did not have the designated wrist band on. If you are looking for a pampered, exceptionally serviced, secluded and relaxed stay, go to the Boulders in Carefree - a far superior resort, and over this weekend, $40 a night cheaper than the marriott.

<Author>Maxesparents
<Content>Some problems that need to be adressed We stayed two nights at this resort, and there are negative points that need to mentioned:1. This hotel caters mainly to conventioneers and - especially during summer - to local families and kids by offering huge discounts. During our stay, the hotel was overflowing with kids - there must have been 600-700 every day. It is a well known secret that locals staying here have friends sneak in all the time for free to use the room and the pools. You can imagine the noise level by those crowds. This is definitely not a place for adults to relax. We had to change our room after three unsupervised teens started a screaming contest next door. Expect a huge unruly kindergarden, not a resort.2. Parking: The hotel unfortunately allows its staff to use a huge part of the closest parking area. The reason is that management attempts to force you to use the valet service ($ 20 per day). If you decide to do self parking, expect long walks in 110-115 degrees. 3. Service: The food at Tuscany was wonderful (salmon/steak), the service understaffed and extremly slow. The chef de cusine came in person to our table to take our order, as she seemed to recognize the service problems. Thanks, chef!4. Housekeeping: Has problems to get rooms cleaned in time. When returning at 3 or 4 pm, do not expect that your room has been freshened up.For someone looking for a quiet and relaxing stay, there are much better choices in the Scottsdale/Phoenix area.

<Author>JLFERG
<Content>Sizzlin' Resort in Phoenix I spent three nights at this resort while attending a conference with a colleague. We were impressed with the rooms, their size and amenities. Beautiful bathrooms too. Great pools and lush grounds (around the desert foliage). But my favorite part of the resort was all of the little bunnies hopping around. There must be more than 100 of them. They are some of the smallest wild rabbits I have ever seen (and I have seen a lot of them). This resort also has some amazing birds--Great Blue Heron, Black (Midnight) Herons--things I didn't expect to see in the desert, but the manmade bodies of water at the resort seem to beckon them. I've been to a lot of conferences, and I must say that the resort catering company puts on a delicious spread--breakfast, lunch and snacks plus out-of-this world Starbucks coffee service, complete with shakers of cinnamon, chocolate and vanilla and liquid vanilla and caramel so you can make your own flavored lattes. Roy's restaurant lived up to the rest of the change providing fresh from the ocean seafood and topnotch drinks. Blue Sage offers a fitness omelet that was absolutely delicious and made me think I was far from eating health food. I like it so much, I ordered it two of the four days I was there. Blue Sage also makes great salads. Only their lunch menu is skimpy.

<Author>aztravlgrl
<Content>I did not want to leave I became very ecstatic about my visit to this resort when I read the reviews on this website that I felt that I had to do my own review upon return. Well, I'm back and here I am - and I have wonderful things to say about this place!I only stayed here for one night because I am a local resident.. but oh my goodness, it was so wonderful. We requested early check-in and arrived at the resort around 1pm. We were helped promptly (no line) and given the keys to our room. We were on the 4th floor (the infamous free laundry floor) and our room was non-smoking with a King sized bed. The view, even though the front desk clerk said was wonderful, was interrupted by nearby buildings. However, I said we were locals so mountain views aren't really too new to us anyway. The room appeared clean, except for the week-old newspaper and towel on the armoire and the broken nightstand door... otherwise everything else was fine. The bed was WONDERFUL - we slept through the night in peace. We had a spa package through the hotel - a great deal - 2 spa treatments, daily spa access, a room, and breakfast for two at the blue sage all for $289.... not bad. I have nothing but great things to say about the Revive Spa. We received a hot stone treatments and afterwards I used the sauna and steam rooms. There is also a pool in the back. Men and women are split throughout, except for the pool area and the bistro. The staff was very helpful, and there is everything a person needs to relax at this spa. There are also showers stocked with shampoo, conditioner, body wash, shave gel, razors, etc - and mouthwash at the sinks. I loved it so much I came back early this morning (yes, we came back today) to sit in the steam room. I'm thinking about going back just to spend the day there sometime in the future. Last night we ate at the shopping center across the street and had dessert at the Meritage Steakhouse. This morning we had our complimentary breakfast at the Blue Sage which was very filling (we did the buffet). We didn't have time for the lazy river, but it is basically a pool that is about three feet deep with jets to move the tubes along - great attraction for kids. The property is beautiful - even though I am from this area it really felt like a vacation. We enjoyed walking on the trails and over the bridges. The parkinig lot is far away, but if you look around the property, you might find some spaces closer to the room once you're checked in. One more thing: Even though I was there for just a night, it felt like a 3-day vacation! Definitely worth it!Anyway, go to this resort if you want a night away from the everyday stresses of life! :)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>On Target Absolutely the customer centric experience you would expect at a JW hotel! We checked my 82 year old mother into the JW at Desert Ridge in Phoenix for a two night stay during a family gathering because of a lack of space at my home....she ended up staying 5 nights. My mother loved the personalized attention but really appreciated the compassion.Our family took advantage of her stay to enjoy the incredible poolside facilities (water slide, lazy river float experience, tree shaded areas, etc.); my mother put on a bathing suit for the first time in 10-15 years. <Content>OMG, What a Great Place I took the kids to Scottsdale to go shopping on Sunday and we decided at the last minute to go down the night before. We were able to get a room, a good deal in the summer too. When we arrived we were greated by the valet who took our car promptly and unloaded things for us. There were four of us in our party and the room was just a bit small but that was because the beds are small. But we were fine with that and even had a roll away brought up which was nice. We ate dinner at the golf club steak house. Nice but the service was slow a bit and they forgot a lot. It was quite expensive too and we kept feeling like we were being watched or something. You know the feeling, like everyone thinks that you dont belong there. But we ignored that and had a good meal. We swam that night in one of the pool and that was nice and relaxing. While we did that we could hear the live music playing in the patio area which made the moolight even more special. We did use roomservice for night snacks and that was prompt and good. That is 24 hours too. The bathroom was beautiful with a seperate shower and tub. Everything in marble and well stocked. The bath goodies that they give you are wonderful and we had to get some from the spa store to take home so we could have them there too. The beds are very very comfortable and I slept well. However, fitting two people on the bed if they arent children is quite hard. For two adults a King Bed would be best. In the morning we had breakfast at the Blue Sage Restr. on the grounds and that was wonderful and well priced. I will go back there over and over again to eat when we visit. The pool area is nice, however if you are going to swim at night be sure to take your own towel as there are none around the pool area that are clean. In the morning however you can find clean towels and a good place to sit around the lazy river or the pools. The service at the pools is great and prompt. We are going back at the end of the month because we loved it so much. They way that they have laid this property out is wonderful and they have decorated it beautifuly. This is the place that our family will go over and over again.

<Author>Travlin'Bug
<Content>Wonderful Getaway... no need to leave the grounds! My husband  I stayed at this resort in Dec. '05, and it was a wonderful experience... the most luxurious resort we'd ever stayed in. The grounds are immaculate and the aroma is refreshing as you stroll past the herbal gardens. The many pools are incredible, and spread out enough that couples can find a quiet spot to enjoy the Arizona weather on one side of the resort while families are enjoying the the lazy river with the kids on the other side. The views of the mountains are spectacular, and my husband enjoyed the challenging golf course. The restaurants are excellent, many on site, and there is a Starbucks in one of many halls. While we were there, a handbell choir entertained with Christmas Carols one evening; a jazz band the following night. The outdoor fireplaces are a great place to relax in the evening  staffed to serve you if you'd like a coffee by the fire. The spa is equally wonderful and it has it's own private pool reserved for spa guests... a quiet place to relax. The rooms are luxurious and the beds very comfortable; the bathrooms are beautiful and spacious. You don't have to leave the resort for anything... a very pleasing  relaxing getaway. Yet, it is a great location if you choose to venture out  shop in Scottsdale or drive to the mountains... upscale shopping  restaurants are nearby. We will definitely return again, and maybe someday bring the kids to enjoy the pools. You won't be dissappointed!

<Author>ColoradoGolfNut
<Content>Fabulous Marriot Resort My wife and I spent the Easter weekend at the JW Marriot Desert Ridge Spa and Resort. This resort was absolutely fabulous. The outstanding service started the moment we arrived. It was amazing to arrive at 7:30am in morning from a flight, and have a room waiting for you. The staff was superb. Courteous, professional, and most of all, helpful. They went out of their way to ensure you had whatever you needed. The facility was superior. The pools and the lazy river raft ride were clean and inviting, especially after a round of golf on one of the two world class golf courses. The Wildfire Golf Club was truly worth the trip. We enjoyed both the Arnold Palmer and Nick Faldo courses so much that we played 18 holes on one day and 36 holes the next. The Pro Shop staff was always courteous and treated golfers to a memorable golf experience. Everything from cleaning and packing your clubs, to having your cart ready to go in the morning with your clubs already on board. We had a chance to sample all of the restaurants in the resort, all were very good. The Meritage Steak House, Roys, and the Blue Sage all served delicious food in a relaxed resort atmosphere. Especially nice was having a Starbucks right off the lobby of the hotel. More hotels should take note of that feature. Phoenix and the JW Marriot Desert Ridge Spa and Resort are definitely on all of our travel plans for the future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Paradise oasis in the desert The moment I pulled into the grounds of the hotel I was blown away by the size of the resort. Soon as I stepped out of the towncar that took us from the airport I was greeted by the wonderful resort staff who welcomed me to Phoenix. Then the bell staff took my luggage and then up to the room, along the way he was telling us about the area and what to and not do to in Phoenix. I planned a side trip to the Grand Canyon and he even told us the best way to get there. We had a standard room which was very nice for 2 people. Beautiful bathrooms are the norm. Bed is very confortable and easy to fall asleep on. We had a nice view of the grounds on our balcony and was nice just to sit out there and enjoy the weather and ambient sounds of the resort. The hotel restaurants are all great and the food is top notch. I highly recommend the butterfish at Roy's and the Salmon dish at the italian place there (forgot the name). When you get out to the main pool area (which there are a lot of different pools) you get to experience how nice the place really is. There are waterfalls, tons of desert flowers, cacti, etc to look at. There were plenty of chairs available and the area was not overly crowded at all. We were there on the weekend and you still can find a place to sit, even in the afternoon. You can sit anywhere and the staff will come by and take your food and drink order and you can eat right by the pool. The lazy river is great to get out of the hot sun and you can relax in there for hours on end just floating aournd. They even have a waterslide for the kids. I saw all different types of people, families, etc, so everyone is welcome here and kids are not a problem. They have 2 fitness centers, one where you have to pay $10 for that includes other spa services, and a free one, which I used and is better than your average hotel gym. They had 8 new treadmills, ellipitcals, free weight area, bikes, etc. Better weight machines are in the pay gym though. Golf courses are well maintained and very challenging. I do not play golf that much, but it was one of the nicest courses I have played. There are 2 and I played the Faldo one. They have a car rental place in the hotel so you can rent a car, like we did and drive to the Grand Canyon or other places. We were with a group of people who paid for our stay at the hotel, if not I am sure I could not afford the $300 plus a night. It is a bit pricy, but worth the trip. One of the nicest resorts I have ever stayed at!! The only small problem I had was there were a lot of birds flying around. Just watch your food so they do not start picking at it!!

<Content>Easter fun Went for a quick getaway Easter weekend with our 2 kids. Great resort, great weather, great fun. Our kids were in the pools all day, every day. They loved the lazy river, water slide and other pools. Pool food was decent and found prices here at the pool (for food  drink) acceptable. Ate most dinners at Dessert Ridge mall across the street (since our kids don't really appreciate fine dining) which consisted of Mimi Cafe, Rock Bottom Brewery, BJs Brewery (chicago style pizza), and On the Border. There are others too, but that's some of the choices. We did eat dinner one night at the resort at Tuscany (Easter dinner) - it was just ok. There were shortages on Sat  Sun of towels at the pool - for a long time on Saturday. Also, we had probelems not getting towels in our room from the cleaning service, and then when we did, the nightime service would take them away and not replace them. I feel this was an issolated incident though and not respresentative of the overall stay. Our kids participated in the free Easter activities, which were well organized. All in all, a great place  we would return. The only thing I would change, is we had 2 beds and they were doubles, not queens. I don't see why they can't fit queens instead, they have the room and adults traveling with their kids would be more comfortable.

<Author>longtimeresident
<Content>hang out in this beautiful hotel If, like me, one of your hobbies is luxury hotels, you might like to see this one. The grounds and the public areas are georgeous. So many palm trees! We were there during the great weather in March, and the huge hotel lobby was open to the outside pool area, making it feel very spacious and inviting. You can sit around fire pits, near the pool, in the lobby, or back by the golf course. A great hotel for hanging out, and at these high spring prices, you want to and get your money's worth. The lazy river is perfect for kids. The spa is beautiful, and you can spend hours there just relaxing. Just across a street is an upscale shopping center with many restaurants and a grocery store, so it is great for families. The only thing I would not rave about are the rooms - the bathrooms are wonderful, but the rooms themselves are slightly above standard Marriott. But most have incredible views! I have stayed at many nice hotels and this is one of the most pleasant for just spending time.

<Author>HockeyMomNJ
<Content>Beautiful Resort Hotel My husband  I spent 3 nights at his hotel for a business conference he was attending. The hotel is huge and very beautiful! The staff was very attentive although on the second day we did tell the front desk that our coffee maker wasn't working and also that we would like non-down pillows. Neither problem was ever taken care of to our satisfaction. Our room was clean and spacious - the bathroom was enormous! Had lunch one day at the poolside restaurant. Good casual food, reasonably priced. The spa was overpriced for what you got. We each booked massages. My husband was satisfied with his but I don't think I got the quality of massage that I've experienced elsewhere. There's a shuttle bus to take you to the resort condos or across the road to a nice shopping mall. Also a shuttle to take you to the airport. (Not one that you can take from the airport to the hotel, though.) Otherwise you need a car to get anywhere. Taxis turned out to be very expensive. Did not get to try out the lazy river or any of the pools since Phoenix was having unusually cold weather at the time. Overall we would definitely stay there again!

<Author>Cynergy
<Content>Wow!! I don't know when I've ever been this impressed with a hotel/resort. I now have a new gold standard for service. I can't say enough about the pristine facility, the attentive and knowledgeable staff or the quality of offerings. This is a beautiful resort - huge and well-kept with gorgeous grounds, several swimming pool areas and (according to my husband) two top-drawer golf courses. Our room was lovely although nothing outside a standard Marriott or Renaissance room, but the bathroom was stellar - big and well-appointed. Our room was in a back wing, facing the spa building and was extremely quiet and peaceful with the added bonus of great sunset views! Every staff member we came in contact with was very courteous and every one of our questions was answered without hesitation. I've never been treated so well. And I must say a word about the on-site restaurants, at least the three I experienced. Breakfast at Blue Sage was surprisingly good (go for a Mexican breakfast entree - delicious!), lunch at Meritage Steakhouse (on the patio) was delightful and dinner at Roy's was exceptional. This Roy's far surpassed the one on Maui, expecially the ambiance and service, which was enthusiastic and detailed. And I love having Starbucks at my disposal - in the morning and in the evening. And we were surprised at the reasonable dining prices, especially after just being in Las Vegas (where prices are outlandish). This resort has a lot to recommend it - and I do - - highly!

<Content>Beautiful, but pricey My wife and I just spent two nights here for a short getaway to warm weather. My wife works for Marriott, and I stay in hotels over 150 nights a year, so we both have a good basis for comparing hotels to each other. First of all, the resort is beautiful. The gardens are immaculate and go beyond just being pretty. There is just something about a stylish building (that's only 6 stories tall) surrounded by ponds, fountains, pools, lawns, flowers, golf courses, and LOTS of palm trees. You could easily mistake this for a Hawaiian island setting. Our room was above average, overall. It was pretty big, with a large bathroom and bright walls, it was very clean, and there is a hint of some kind of flower perfume that is pleasant when you walk in. I was surprised that for $500 a night, though, that guests still have to pay $10 daily if they want internet access. You can stay at Courtyard by Marriott for under $100 w/ free internet.The pools were very warm at 86 degrees, and the Lazy River was nice and relaxing. There seems to be lots and lots of space for guests at the pools - hundreds of lounge chairs. The fitness center is great - all new equipment, including cardio w/ individual televisions, free weights, and machines.All of the hotel staff was very professional and pleasant. We ate at Roy's one night and off-property for all other meals. Roy's was nothing to write home about. We had eaten at the one in Pebble Beach, which was very good, but this one was about a 7 out of 10. We ordered the appetizer sampler platter, and everything was delicious, though pricey at $25. The entrees we ate were two of Roy's signature dishes - macadamia nut encrusted mahi-mahi w/ lobster Cognac sauce and soy-glazed butterfish. Both fish were cooked well and tasted good, but lacked depth of flavor. They was no explosion of flavors in the mouth. So, the meal was good, but not outstanding in my opinion. Service was very slow every step of the way, from taking our order, to getting a drink, to getting dessert (it took over 30 minutes even though we ordered the souffle with our dinner order, as recommended on the menu). They came around early on and gave us each 1 breadroll (yum!), but despite my requests for another roll, we never saw the bread guy again the entire night.There are plenty of places to eat near the hotel, if you don't want to go fancy all the time. We spent a whole day in Old Town Scottsdale. We highly recommend a sundae at The Sugar Bowl and authentic Mexican food at Los Olivos.So, I think the Marriott is a very nice hotel, but probably a bit pricey for the average traveler, espescially considering the cost of eating on-site.  
<Date>Feb 14, 2006

<Author>stonemanmb
<Content>Best Hotel in Scottsdale My Girlfriend and I stayed at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge the week between Christmas and New Years in December. We couldn't have been any happier with it. From the moment we got there, we were treated like royalty. The hotel is gorgeous, and the water/fire/earth/sky motif is just amazing. So many waterfalls and fountains around, it just feels so relaxing. After getting to our first room, we decided that since we'd be staying for a week, we would like a room with a better view, and they gladly gave us one overlooking the botanical gardens and the driving range. The restaurants are delicious, and it was a treat to sit by the pool and enjoy a margarita and the cobb salad.The golf is a little pricey ($190/round), so we decided to use the driving range each day. We couldn't have had a better time.There are so many shops in close proximity to the resort, we felt like we were in heaven.The Spa is amazing, and to fully enjoy it you need to spend the entire day there. We had lunch, sat by the pool, and got a couples massage. It was all AMAZING!The only downside was that on the day we checked out, we were awakened by a fire alarm at 4am. We had to scurry outside, and the desert air is mighty crisp that early! This is the nicest resort we have ever stayed in, and we will come back again and again.

<Author>bdouty
<Content>Mixed feelings We just stayed at the Desert Ridge from 12/27 to 1/01.We had picked it over the Biltmore based on reviews here. It met but did not exceed our expectations. Big hotel, nice facilities but starting to show wear after only three years. Pretty crowded and noisy (Fiesta Bowl attendees) - good for families but not for couples who want a romantic getaway. Rooms nice but nothing special - beds could be improved. Service above average overall, especially in Cloud Club (but you're paying extra so it should be better). My husband is a serious golfer and gives good marks to both courses. But as a first time visitor to Phoenix, I must say I don't know what the attraction is other than the weather. Wasn't overly impressed by anything I saw there. Took a day trip to Sedona - that was impressive, especially views at Enchantment resort(and that gets spotty reviews). Tuscany restaurant meal very enjoyable, but at the Meritage steakhouse they were just about throwing the food at us. And I just wish people would learn to dress in something other than jeans in nicer resort restaurants. Nice break from Minneapolis weather, but I don't know if I'd return. My husband will, but year-round golf is the attraction for him.

<Content>wonderful stay JW Desert Ridge We recently stayed with our family for Thanksgiving weekend at the JW Desert Ridge. <Author>gogoyeeha
<Content>Had Great Experience Very Happy We stayed at JW Marriot Desert Ridge Resort for three nights in mid-November 2005. This is a beautiful resort with excellent grounds and rooms. Check in was smooth and the room we received was in a very good location, just steps from the exercise room and the 鈥渓azy river鈥?pool, and in close proximity to the main pool and the lobby areas. The room was ground floor, with a patio overlooking gardens and the golf course. A room one or two floors higher, with balcony, would have afforded a better view, but we were happy with ours. The room was very large, with king size bed, sofa, coffee table, two chairs, desk, television cabinet, and a huge marble/tile bathroom with both tub and separate shower (glass enclosed). The bathroom amenities were top-notch. The room was immaculate when we checked in and stayed that way while we were there. The room also included a digital safe and small fridge to the side of the mini-bar. The only complaint at all about the room is that the fridge did not keep things real cold, just cool. We had a small ice chest with us so things we wanted to be really cold we just iced down.The resort is quite large and spread out, so be prepared to walk. While valet parking is offered, it is not mandatory and self parking is available. It is quite a walk from the self park lot to the room wings so people that have mobility problems should be aware of that.The exercise room by the pool area is open 24 hours and is very well equipped with state of the art equipment. It was busy while we were there, but early morning visits usually found open treadmills. The spa was very nice and offers the typical services. It also has another pool available, but one must pay a daily spa fee to use it. This might be worth it when the resort is full of kids but while we were there we say maybe 4 children. There is also another exercise room located adjacent to the spa, but it is not open 24 hours.The grounds and the public areas are very nice. There are several dining options available in the resort, as well as a Starbucks for coffee drinks. There is of course lots of out door dining space. The bars at the main pool and the lazy river offer a wide selection of drinks (reasonably priced for a resort) and a nice selection of food (also not priced too badly) and make a nice place for a pool side lunch. We ate dinner at the resort only one evening, at Roy鈥檚, which was excellent. It was expensive but worth every cent. We both chose the fixed price menu which is good value at $33. It offers a very nice selection of Roy鈥檚 specialties served in three courses. Roy鈥檚 also has a nice wine list and offers some fairly inexpensive house wines (which were quite good) by the glass. We highly recommend Roy鈥檚.Just outside the gate of the resort is the Desert Ridge Shopping Center which offers a wide variety of dining options and many shops. Hint: if you want to buy liquor, beer or wine to stock the room, Osco Drugs is MUCH cheaper than the Albertsons Grocery store.Marriot offers a free shuttle to and from the shopping center so you could leave your car parked at the hotel. It runs until fairly late in the evening.We really enjoyed our stay and rate this hotel as excellent. We were able to relax around the pools, have some good food and drinks, and just chill, which we both badly needed. We found nothing to complain about at all and would not hesitate to return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it! We really enjoyed our stay at this resort. Our package included free breakfast which was wonderful. We had a choice between the buffet or menu items. I chose the buffet which consisted of made to order omelettes, pancakes, and waffles. There were also many other pre-prepared hot and cold items to choose from. The resort itself is beautiful and makes you feel like you're miles and miles away from home. There was live entertainment in the evenings so you could sit outside and enjoy it. Roy's restaurant is excellent. It is open for dinner only. I recommend the Blackened Ahi Tuna and the chocolate souffle. It was so good that we had dinner there two nights in a row. The pools were crowded during the day, but it was too hot for us to be by the pools during the day anyway. We used the hot tubs and pools at night which was nice since it was less crowded. The fitness center was great. I especially liked that it was open 24 hours and there weren't any hidden resort fees to use the fitness center.My favorite part was Revive Spa. The facility is absolutely gorgeous. Treatment includes full use of the facility which includes a fitness center, steam room, showers, jacuzzi, sauna, as well as a beautiful outdoor pool and spa. There is a cute little restaurant that you can have lunch at after your massage. We actually had lunch in our robes and slippers. There is also a relaxation room that you can enjoy before and after your treatment. I had a Swedish massage one time and a Hot Stone Massage another time. I was not impressed with the Hot Stone Massage. Mainly because my therapist took too much time to prepare the stones which took away from my massage time.Lastly, the room itself was nice, very clean and comfortable. We had a beautiful view of the golf course.This is an expensive hotel, but there are great seasonal packages. We have been to many resorts and this is one of my favorites. I can't wait to return!  
<Date>Nov 15, 2005

<Author>dobie102977
<Content>Mixed bag I just returned from Phoenix and a stay at the JW. Still conflicted on my feelings regarding our stay. My husband was out there for a conference and it just happened that our anniversary was the day after the conference ended. So I flew out a few days after he did and we just extended our stay. Overall I enjoyed it. The grounds are breathtaking! The food is great and everyone is very friendly. I really liked the location because it was located between Phoenix and Scottsdale and close to the freeway. It made getting around very easy. The staff was very helpful and always had smiles on their faces. Like I've already said the grounds are amazing. I really can't say enough about that and it really made up for the bad things (I'll get to those). There is a patio just outside the lobby that has several tables and lounge chairs with firepits and it was always the place to be in the evening and early morning. I really enjoyed taking a book and just hanging out. The pools are very nice and never seemed crowded.Okay so here are the few negatives. The pools weren't heated and it wasn't very comfortable to swim. However, this was in November. Second, I called two weeks in advance and spoke with someone at the hotel. I explained that my husband was going to be there for the conference but that I would be flying in halfway through the week for our anniversary. I told her it would be great if we could get a room with a good view and a king sized bed. When my husband got there he was put in a room with doubles. He told the front desk I would be there in 3 days for our anniversary and could they move him as soon as a king came available. So when I arrived 3 days later he was still in the doubles. We slept in seperate beds because I am 5 months pregnant and there was NO way we could both squeeze into one of those little beds. Not ideal on a romantic getaway. The next day we called and again requested a king room. We were called back around noon and were told our new room was ready and a bellman was on his way up to move us. We loaded everything up and made the trek across the hotel to our new room. When we opened up the door it was another double but the view was amazing (pools). The bellman called the front desk and explained we were wanting a king and again said it was for our anniversary. He was told which room to take us to but it was on the 3rd floor and overlooked the front drive! Not exactly romantic but we opted for the king vs. the view. This was the biggest problem we had. I know the hotel was sold out because of conferences. However, it just seems to me that someone would've thought to put more of the single business travelers into the doubles and leave the king rooms for couples. Also, over the course of a week can you really tell me there wasn't a king room with a decent view that came available. Also, my husband is a preferred Marriott reward holder. So much for rewarding loyalty that week.We did make the best of it and really enjoyed ourselves. Overall it was nice. Just a few little annoying things that keep me from giving it an Excellent. Not sure if we'd stay again. If we knew the room situation would be better we would. However, because of the volume of conferences that seems unlikely.

<Content>Lovely grounds and great breakfast buffet Spent two days at this resort. Very clean and grounds were lovely. Got the package one night that included a full breakfast. Breakfast was anything on the menu and included a buffet which was pretty much anything you can imagine-freshly made omelets, pancakes, many breakfast meats, potatoes and delicious fruit, not to mention sweets etc! The meals at the resort were expensive and a bit more expansive than we really wanted to eat. Starbucks on premises which was a nice touch as I like their coffee. The room is nice, nothing out of this world but comfy bed and very clean. Ask for a pool side room as they are the best. Do not get a room around the Isle of Capri unless you want to look at the most lifeless view in the resort. No color, no interest. We will try another resort on our next visit.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>wonderful family resort!!! Our family of five had a fantastic experience at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge.Even before we arrived i was impressed with the staff -- especially Cookie at the conciege desk. She was extremely helpful, kind and professional as she made recommendations and reservations for us for dinner as well as excursions.Check-in was a breeze - the porters were quick and helpful. Our room was very clean with a large bathroom. The kids loved the balcony which had beautiful desert views and overlooked a golf course. The grounds were beautifully maintained and the pools were a HUGE hit especially the lazy river! Since we have three young children we decided to use their valet service -- well worth the money as it quite a hike to the parking lots. The valets were always friendly and attentive.We ate poolside one afternoon and everything was fresh and delicious. We appreciated the chilled lemon water in the lobby which was so refreshing given the temperatures stayed around 112 degrees during our vacation.One excursion we went on was a desert tour via Hummer with Stellar Adventures. Our guide was fantastic - very knowledgeable about the indigenous plant and animal life and very friendly and helpful.Take time to go to DC Ranch - a planned community not far form the resort - great restaurants Eddie V's and San Felipe's Cantina.The Arizona Science Center was amazing -- we could have stayed all day. Wonderful, fun, educational and interactive activities for the kids ( adults)!As we headed to the airport, the kids were already asking when we could go back to the resort - always a good sign of a great vacation.

<Content>Great resort!! This is an absolutely beautiful resort. I took a solo trip to the resort in July 2005 for some much needed rest and relaxation. The rooms are clean, pretty, and nicely sized. <Content>Beautiful Place We just came back from the JW Marriott last night on Sept 6th we were there for labor day weekend. This place is really beautiful considering 106 deg weather everyday. By the way you def dont need to rent a car there is a market place accross the street. 5 dollar cab ride. They have everything you need there, restaurants, shopping, drug store, target, malls everything. If you want to go a little further like 15 minutes or so there are some really elite restaurants. I forgot the name but it was seafood and very good, pricey but worth it. My only issue was that night we got there 2:45am some kids pulled the fire alarm waking the whole hotel. It took like 25 minutes for them to shut the alarm which was annoying but it was just a false alarm. It wasn't that great that all that was done was management left a notice under our doors that morning to apolize for the inconvience. Free breakfast would have been better then just a stupid note. But over all this was a beautiful place and if I came back I would definitly get out of the hotel and see more.

<Author>oxnrd123
<Content>Loved the J.W. Marriott Desert Ridge We were there during the first week of August for four nights. When we got there it was 3:30 and we were able to check in. They gave us a room in the fourth floor (where the complimentary washer and driers(2) are) with a great view into the patio and the pools. It was great. The hotel has activities schedule daily some are free others at a cost. The concierge desk was a great help. They have suggestions on places to visit and most important direct directions. What they say in the other reviews is true. This is certainly another type of heat. We were able to go to different places(Old Town Scottsdale, Slide Rock, Sedona, Heard Museum) because it really doesn't feel that bad. Well the hotel is spectacular. They told us that the hotel wasn't that busy that week but we still saw that the lazy river was pretty full. The pools are really nice and we were able to find chairs and there were plenty of towels available. The lazy river has a slide and plenty of adults were enjoying it. The kids menu is a steal for $4 you really get a huge serving. Most of our dining was away from the hotel since we did visit other sites away from the hotel during the early mornings. We would come back to the hotel around 3:00 and would hit the pools till after dark. Pools close around 11:00 p.m. Something that was not mentioned in this site is that during the summer months it's monsoon season in AZ. This means that late in the evenings lightning could strike and then it could rain which means you can't be in the outdoor patios enjoying the music being played or in the water. For one of the nights we were there we had one of these storms. We went to our room to change out of our swimming attire and just when we were on our way downstairs the entire hotel lost power for about a half hour but the power did restore pretty quick. The weather changed rather quickly. It's true that across from the hotel is a mall with restaurants and even an arcade called Jillians. We really enjoyed our stay there. The lazy river was super fun for the kids and the pools are all very nice and not that deep at most four feet. All in all I recommend this hotel... we definetely plan to go back soon!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Time My husband and I just returned from spending 4 nights at the Desert Ridge Marriott for a conference. Beautiful hotel and great staff! I hope this review doesn't sound negative but if we had paid the standard room rate, I probably would have been a little disappointed.We were able to check in early which was very nice so we could enjoy our first day out by the pools and lazy river. The guest rooms were decorated nicely and the beds were very comfortable!! There were a couple little maintenance things that could have been overlooked in our room but it really didn't make a difference in our stay. One of the lightbulbs was out in our bathroom and part of the shower handle was coming off the wall a little. Our room was on the fifth floor and when the bellman took us through the hallways, it was very warm. But maybe, that is to be expected in Phoenix in August. The air conditioning wasn't on in our room when we checked in so it took an hour or so to cool off.One of the things that I really thought wasn't very appealing was the carpeting in the hallways of our wing, in quite a few areas it seemed to be dirty. Inside one entrance out to the parking lot, there were dried flowers or leaves on the floor that were there the entire four days we stayed. I kinda thought that would have been cleaned up as soon as it was noticed by the staff.The lobby was beautiful and very clean though! All the beautiful marble and large windows overlooking the back of the hotel. There was always iced tea and water available to the guests. At night, it is absolutely beautiful on the grounds, torches lit along the pathways and fire pits with comfy chairs and table all over.We enjoyed our visit to the spa tremendously! The Revive Spa was a beautiful building. The private spa pool was a very relaxing place to enjoy the rest of the afternoon after our massages. If I were to suggest to anyone coming to the Marriott Desert Ridge, ask for a room other than in Wing A if you have a car. While walking out to the parking lot from this wing, you walk past the garbage area and there is a strong sewer and garbage odor there.Like I said earlier, if we had paid the standard rate I would have been just a little bit disappointed but we were really able to overlook these little issues and still had a wonderful time!!

<Author>iyhberry
<Content>This JW is VERY nice! Highly Recommended! July in Phoenix? Who goes to Phoenix in the midst of a never ending heat wave? We did and WE LOVED IT!! The hotel is beautiful. It still feels new--after three years of service. We had a large suite (Rm 4222) and decided to splurge on the Cloud Club Access--which by the way--is absolutely worth every since penny--a lovely, abundant breakfast buffet....delicious appetizers....open bar in the evenings....lovely sitting areas....the Cloud Club was our favorite feature aside from....THE LAZY RIVER. The LR was wonderful. We spent at least 5 hours per day in the LR...sipping the Kokopelei (sp?) Cabana Coladas that the nice pool attendants were happy to deliver to our spot. It鈥檚 not five hours in the pool...its five hours of heaven....with a purpose...there is a current...there is a water slide...the lazy river made us forget that the outside temp was 110. The LR by mid-afternoon gets rather crowded (almost too crowded)...but we did not let this stop our enjoyment...rather it was noted...The Lazy River is now crowded. Good thing we have our rafts already. Let's keep on going.We used the Spa workout area. It was nice. The regular gym had a little bit of high school locker room smell--which happens when people work out....but we found the Spa Gym a bit less crowded. We loved walking around the outside common areas of the hotel at night. The environs are beautiful. The torches (yes, torches in the summer) all around the main lawn. The outside lounges and restaurants and live music created a tranquil but not dull....a relaxing, lively....beautiful spot....There were lots of kids. We were travelling without kids and were not overwhelmed by their presence. The resort is large. We did not golf or do much else besides eat and spend time in the lazy river...and we were PERFECTLY content. Overall, the service of the hotel staff was top notch. We loved our room. We did not leave the hotel for 4 days and we didn't want to....we felt spoiled every minute and will definitely be coming back!
