<Author>Daisymom
<Content>Lots of fun at the Desert Ridge! I just returned from 6 nights at the JW Marriott Desert Ridge with my husband and two children (4,7). We had a fabulous time there - spending the majority of it in the pool areas. We loved the lazy river. My kids preferred not using a tube but just free floating. My 4 year old wore a ski life vest and was able to safely float, too. The resort is very beautiful, especially at night. The many pool areas are nice so that everyone can find a pool that is their speed. One pool we called the quiet pool because it is off to the side a bit and was used very little. We were, however, disappointed with the poolside service. During 6 days there we always had to wave down a waiter to get them to come by. Very few servers would stop by and say, Can I get you anything?. Once they took our first order, we would usually receive fine service. Poolside food is pretty good. Kids meals are a deal at $4 with soda, fries, and entree. My kids ended up sharing one since they were good size. The Cobb is great and huge! We were also surprised that the poolside service and bar close at between 6:00 and 7:00 pm.The rooms were spacious and nice. Our view over the front courtyard area was nice because the city lights at night were gorgeous. During the evenings we often sat out on the patio (Vista Lounge) and listened to the music, had drinks, ate off the small appetizer menu and watched our kids play for hours on the grassy area with several other children. They had a blast and it worked for us. Our overall experience was great, though I did not feel we received great service in any area. I was never told about many of the perks at resort and only knew of them because of TripAdvisor. For example, the complimentary laundry on the 4th floor, the free shuttle to the mall area, the gym, spa specials, etc. We would definitely come back to the resort with our children. For my husband and I, we might try an adult oriented resort that is more focused on service.  
<Date>Jul 23, 2005

<Author>FWCOrlando
<Content>All in all a great choice We were looking for an upscale resort that would let my wife and I enjoy some of the offerings of a resort while allowing the kids to be kids (who are 5 and 3). The JW Marriott at Desert Ridge is an excellent choice. Let me start with saying that the service personnel from check in to the poolside service to housekeeping were friendly, helpful and courteous. The resort itself is beautiful with many pools to fit whatever age group is interested. The lazy river was a nice feature for all ages. A large grass area in the center of the resort allowed kids to run and run. I saw kids playing there from morning until night. The rooms were nice and spacious and the balcony a nice touch. It allowed us to put our kids to sleep at a decent hour and continue to enjoy drinks on the balcony that overlooked the outdoor seating and band. We felt like we were part of the nightlife without having to leave the room. Once you closed the sliding door to your room is sufficiently cut out the noise from the outside. The outdoor Desert Ridge Mall which is adjacent to the Marriott property ( the resort faces away from this) was extremely convenient to access the 30 or so restaurants which offered a nice variety of prices and food choices. It even had a Target for those last minute items you did not bring (actually knowing its there we would have just bought some things when we got there). This location of Desert Ridge is north of Phoenix and convenient to 17 that allowed us day trips to the Grand Canyon, Sedona and Verde Canyon. It was 110 to 113 degrees during our trip but what they say is true, its a different kind of heat.One small negative, the view of the resort from the rooms is great but the view of nearby mountains was limited.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it.. Paradise The staff was exceptional. Everything I asked for was granted. The only suggestion I would give is to have an adults only pool built. I don't know what the guy with kids expected. The hotel was full of families this Memorial Week and the kids were happy. They had a special area for entertaining them. Kids are parent's responsibility. If you wish to travel with your spouse and have a romantic vacation, leave the kids with the grandparents or maybe go to a club Med. This hotel does give the kids great importance.. perhaps I wish there were less of them.. since mine are now adults. The kids there were happy and enjoying themselves. There was a children program, but you had to pay a fee. Again I remind parents that this hotel is not a children only daycare center.. it is a large resort and most of the time has large adult conventions.. Around Memorial weekend we had the Pediatric Nurses Convention.Food: Roy's was excellent.. Drew our waiter was fabulous as was the Manager that night.. she knew we were celbrating a 50th Birthday and gave us a quiet area in the patio overlooking the grounds. We felt as though we were in Hawaii... even had a lovely breeze.The breakfast/lunch restaurant was great also. We did utilize the Cloud Room facilities and the staff catered to all our wishes.. by the way, the chocolate chip cookies were fabulous. Also, if you wish coffee and don't see it .. ask the ladies for some... whatever you want.. ask them for it.. they were amazing.Pool: there were always chairs. We positioned ourselves by a tree facing the water way and if you wish an umbrella, ask the pool employees, they will bring one to you.I have stayed at the Westin Kierland and enjoyed it.. but this hotel was like being tucked away on vacation in an island. I loved it!PS.. We will return.

<Author>vmarshcpa
<Content>Decent enough-long distance between guest rooms and conference facilities The room was quite nice but I would never have paid that much on my own if my employer hadn't paid for the conference. Beautiful property and close to nearby restaurants and shopping. Conference facilities were nice but only complaint was the sheer distance between room and conference facilities---took me over 10 minutes to get to and from if I walked at a quick pace. I liked having a nice view of the desert. Restaurants close a little early during the week (10:00). I was still staying in Phoenix elsewhere later in the week and drove back to check out Roy's Restaurant-Hawaiian Fusion. They were very accomodating with reservations and food was great. We loved the fire pits to relax by and it has a lot of ambiance. I wouldn't pay the high cost for the room if I were traveling for pleasure---rooms weren't THAT special so I was glad that conference rate was about half rack rate. Only other thing is that I had to ask three times to have my Marriott number added to my reservation---I finally got it added at the front desk after I had checked out. Valet service was friendly and reliable and was validated at Roy's.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Outstanding Resort I've been very underwhelmed by other Marriott Resorts I've stayed in over the last few years ... but not here!!!. This is a fabulous resort in every manner. I'll break it down:Property ... could not ask for any more. The location is not great ... in the middle of nowhere. However, the resort itself is practically made of marble. Everything is new, spotless, impressive etc. The pool complex is absolutely unreal. We loved all the pools, especially the lazy river. The property outside impeccably managed ... full of flowers, waterfalls, palm trees etc. Always the sound of relaxing soft music everywhere, as they have speakers throughtout all the garden areas.Rooms ... Very average. Marble baths are nice. Not the highlight of the hotel. View from main building was unbelievable. All rooms have balcony's, refridgerators etc.Service ... Perfect (not too much or too little) and always with a smile. I've been to scores of resorts and hotels as I travel a lot and never felt so welcomed. Everything was right on time and to our specification. Tips seemed appreciated in return for good work, not expected. Maids, front desk, bell, wait staff, and valet all took the time to say good morning and play with our 1 year old.Recreation ... Pools are the highlight as discussed earlier. The Wildfire Golf Club has two courses, Faldo and Palmer. I thought the Faldo was OK. I'm not a fan of the overbunkered type of course. I've played better desert layouts. Everything was well maintained and in great condition though and service was outstanding. A little pricy at $150, but that does include range, cart and 6 Calloway balls.Food ... There are 4 real restaurants ... the others are really casual, patio type snack bars. Roy's was outstanding (I mean top level outstanding). Blue Sage was average / good. We didn't eat in Tuscany or Meritage but I heard both were very good. The pool bar serves great lunches ... we ate lunch there every day. The have outstanding salads (Cobb is awesome) and great wraps. We went offsite a few nights.Spa ... My wife said it was incredible. I was wondering if she would ever come back.The resort does a great job with young children. Although it does cater to business meetings, we hardly even saw them even though there was a huge one in the hotel. It is very large and plenty of space for all. Pool and restaurants not really crowded, even though hotel had high capacity.All in all ... If you want a desert vacation ... you can't go wrong here. Not as scenic as some other places (Camelback resorts, Phoenician etc.), but everything else scores highly.  
<Date>Apr 20, 2005

<Author>MisstheDogs
<Content>Excellent Resort I stayed at the resort both as a member of a group and then as a single guest. Overall, I was very impressed. In particular, the staff was exceptional. Just walking by, staff would greet me. And, there was always plenty of staff in every venue for both group events and for single travelers.I don't GOLF or play TENNIS, so can't comment on the courses or courts.The POOLS were very nice. There are several pools, including the lazy river, in which you float around on tube rafts. Great for kids and adults who are young at heart. Also a water slide, primarily used by kids. Many pool chairs -- even on a very crowded day, it was easy to find a chair. Towels are plentiful as is ice water with lemon. They provide pitchers and replenish as needed. Pool service (bar/food) is decent and generally fairly priced -- although margaritas at $8 apiece are a bit pricey.I sampled three RESTAURANTS -- Roy's, Tuscany, and Blue Sage. Food was best at Roy's -- excellent for the price. However, they have a practice of requiring single diners to eat at the bar or chef's counter rather than at tables (even when the restaurant isn't crowded), which was disappointing. The service at Tuscany was first rate but the food was only average. Blue Sage for breakfast and appetizers was OK. Food provided during the convention was good. Service was outstanding. They set up enough food stations and bars so that, even with an extremely large group, we never had to wait in line for food or drinks. Dirty plates were cleared quickly. The Revive SPA is excellent. High class service throughout. One of the best massages I've ever had. Facial was ok. I would note that the prices are steep, even based on the East Coast norm. You get what you pay for but you will pay for it.ROOMS are nice and reasonably large. I would guess that every room has a decent view. All have balconies or patios. Big TV. Robes. Minibar. Good sized bathroom, with separate shower  tub. Toiletries (e.g., shampoos) are replenished frequently. Only problem is that soundproofing could be improved.STAFF is excellent. They were very supportive of a large group yet very attentive of individuals. I felt that everyone I met went out of his/her way to make my stay pleasant and enjoyable. People seemed genuinely happy to be working there.The property is deceptively large. Although there are nearly 900 rooms, you don't feel either claustrophobic with your fellow conventioneers or isolated if you're not with a convention. I would definitely recommend this for business meetings. Everything ran without a hitch. I would not hesitate to stay on as a single traveler. However, given the size of the property, if traveling solely for vacation purposes, I would probably stay at a smaller, more intimate resort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful and Relaxing The JW Marriott Desert Ridge Resort is an outstanding accommodation for business and pleasure. My husband and I stayed for a business conference March 30-April 2, 2005 and enjoyed it tremendously. Only about a half hour drive from airport. The hotel is just beautiful with impressive marble entry and a fountain. Our room with balcony overlooked about 5 different pools, lazy river, golf course and palm trees. Restaurants have excellent service and delicious food, especially enjoyed Meritage. The property is well manicured and pristine. Staff was friendly and courteous. I rented a convertible from Hertz (on property) and had a great time driving 20 min. to Scottsdale and on to Tempe for a day trip. Perfect weather at 82 degrees and great time of year to visit. We don't golf but everyone we spoke to thought it was wonderful. We would like to visit again with the children, they would love the pools and lazy river. I would highly recommend this property!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Okay hotel for a meeting I recently stayed here 2 nights for a meeting. The hotel is in the middle of nowhere, although there is a shopping center across the highway. It looks like a giant, sprawling pueblo. Every room has a Holiday Inn-like balcony (a small slab of concrete with 2 plastic chairs). My room was large and comfortable, with all the usual amenities such as 27 flat screen TV. The beds were disappointingly soft for a hotel of this price range. The bathroom was very large, with separate bathtub and shower stall and wonderfully plush towels. However, the showerhead was fixed, and it was impossible to properly wash your lower body. The MAJOR problem was the noise from the atrium, which came through loudly at night. Definitely ask for a quiet room that is NOT on the atrium.

<Author>Jannel43
<Content>Stunning hotel, great service. We just returned from five days there and we thoroughly enjoyed our stay. Despite the fact that the hotel was massive and also that it was sold out, we never encountered lines or glitches in service. Also, the hotel is extremely quiet. I expected to hear the many children staying there (including ours!), but I just didn't. Also the onsite restaurants were all very good and while Roy's was always packed, the steakhouse and the fine Italian place were nearly empty and still served exceptional food. The service was flawless everywhere.On the negative side, we were able to get one standard room (tried to get a second one, but it was too late), and the four of us were packed in like sardines. The trundle bed which was brought in was quite comfortable, but took up valuable living space. The bathroom was huge -- maybe we should have put the trundle bed in there!Secondly, this hotel is remote. We nearly broke the bank being driven to spring training baseball games and the airport. While we loved this resort, if we returned to Phoenix for spring training we would definitely search for a more centrally located property.

<Author>wirepaladin08
<Content>Quite a place but off the beaten track Stayed at Marriott's Desert Ridge Resort for a weekend in March. The rooms are quite nice and well appointed. Every room has a balcony. This is an enormous resort -- around a thousand rooms. The resort caters to major conventions and meetings. Just know that in advance. Also be aware that it is in the far north portion of Phoenix. Phoenix has grown by leaps and bounds in recent years and traffic is a mess so beware if you have to drive far.Staff is friendly and accomodating with the exception of the golf course marshall, who seemed to have a chip on his shoulder for some unknown reason. Maybe he was just having a bad day.The hotel is surrounded by two golf courses - a Palmer course and a Faldo course. The Faldo course is difficult and heavily bunkered. Both were in exceptional condition.Pools are great. Nice fitness area. The resort spends a fortune on landscaping and fountains and it shows. Nicely done.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous experience I and my wife stayed at the JW Desert Ridge for 2 nights during the thanksgiving break and had a great time. They gave us a room overlooking the pool and the mountain preserve (a room on the south side will get you this) and it was simply beautiful. The service is impeccable, the house keeprs won't bother you until late, the servers by the pool are always hospitable and there to bring you anything you want. I'd highly recommend this Hotel and if we ever go back to Phoenix we know where we are going back to stay. BTW, the Hotel is also quite kid friendly (we were surpised to see quite a few kids enjoying the lazy river. The pools were very clean though a bit cold (despite the water being at 82), so we used the 2 outdoor jacuzzis instead. During the evenings, the patio has beautiful outdoor fireplaces where guests mingle and there is live music. All in all, it was a wonderful experience. The view in the evenings of the tall Palms and the outdoor Patio is incredible. Highly recommended.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>5 star... I don't think so. If your a true user of 5 star Luxury Resorts such as Four Seasons and Ritz Carltons, then you'll be disappointed in this one. Just got back from this resort (Nov. 2004) and booked it because of the reviews on line, but very disappointed all around.Rooms are average and the bathroom after reading the reviews was very disappointing. Only one sink and not very large at that. Eventhough there is a sperate shower stall, it was so on top of the toilet that when you opened the shower door you just miss the toilet by about 2 inches. One day I had the call front desk to get my room cleaned. This was after 2:00 pm the day after I checked in. I was told they were busy because a lot of guest checked out and new ones were arriving and they needed to turn over the rooms. So I quess that means I was put on the back burner since I was already checked in. Staff were ok, but not 5 star helpful or even 5 star friendly. Beware major conventioneers at this hotel. In fact the week I was there the hotel was 95% booked and probably 80% of quest were there on conventions. They litterly take over the hotel. One night the only lobby lounge in the hotel was taken over by these conventioneers and there was no place to sit and have a quite drink. Also a hugh TV screen was brought in so all the men could watch Monday night football, for which they proceeded to behave as typical male's would during a football game. I think you know what I mean. Another evening most of the pool area and hot tub section was closed off for a private convention dinner party.This type of service would not happen in a true 5 star resort. The Marriott is trying to match the Ritz Carltons and Four Seasons, but are falling short. Remimber conventioneers do not pay out of their pockets for these trips, their corporations do. They could care less about your hard earned vacation.All in all not worty of a 5 star rating. Spend a couple of dollars more and stay at the Phoenician or Four Seasons. Much more worth your hard earn dollar.

Although we had initially planned to divulge in a spa service, none of us wanted to leave the beautiful outdoors and all passed. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A great resort We just got back from a quick 3 night stay (10/7-10/10 at this resort. We had reserved two rooms and requested connecting rooms via email and also by fax, but upon check in they said they hadn't taken care of it. They were apologetic and Roxanne said she would take care of it the next morning. She came through (Thanks Roxanne!) and the next day we had connecting rooms of which one was the standard deluxe room connected to a luxury suite which was perfect for our family. This is a great time of year, the weather was still in the high 90's but the crowded pools I've read about in previous reviews was non-existent on both Thursday and Friday. Saturday there were more people around the pools but there was plenty of room to sit wherever you wanted and hardly anyone was in any of the pools. Almost everyone was just sunbathing.They have 4 pools, a lazy river with a water slide, a long narrow j-shaped pool, a standard rectangular pool, and another large pool with a huge water drencher at the end of it. They also have two hot tubs, one for 15 people, the other holds 26 people.The resort has a Starbucks on site as well as several other restaurants. I read previously that turn down service was non-existent, but we did have turn down service every night although one night it wasn't until 830pm.There are two washers and dryers on the 4th floor which are complimentary as is the detergent and Bounce. Depending on your group the mall across the street probably isn't within walking distance. We have a 9 and 3 year old so it wasn't for us. From our room it was probably a good HOT mile from room to mall. The mall is nice though not enclosed and is spread out.Staff was very attentive and friendly, the grounds were very impressive, lots of water mixed in with the desert surroundings.We definitely would go back!

<Author>beenthereseenthat
<Content>Worthy of 5-Star but beware... It's a deluxe resort  spa, no argument. The deluxe room was spacious, the bathroom opulent with separate marble + glass shower and comfy bathtub. The restaurants pricey, but the food presentation and quality does match. The outdoor seating is very attractive, surrounded by lush gardens and water features. The grounds are well looked after. All rooms have a view of some sort, the least preferred would be the rooms looking west, across the front entrance, although the sunsets from that vantage point are outstanding.Other views are across the golf course to the South and North, and the best view, from what I observed, would be over the pools, gardens and golf course, to the east.While the resort is deluxe, the type of guests staying can range, and you may be exposed to noisy, obnoxious, and unwanted behaviour. Not the hotel's fault, mind you, but might affect your enjoyment all the same. Lots of cell phone activity at this resort since it is a conference site. Also, lots of kids...so, you might not get the quiet relaxation you're seeking. The Spa is outstanding with its own swimming and exercise facilities (additional charge) but well worth the additional fee(s). The staff (associates) in all areas understand customer satisfaction and everyone is friendly and efficient to deal with.I would return to this hotel under the right circumstances.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great stay over Labor Day Weekend! I stayed at the JW Marriott for two nights over Labor Day weekend with my boyfriend. The grounds are beautiful, the room itself was not remarkable (average) but the bathrooms w/glass door shower and marble floors was nice, food at Roy's great (def go with the price fixe menu and they make great dirty martini's), Blue Sage breakfast buffet is a must (blue corn pancakes and tons of fresh fruit), the pools were large and nice (but lazy river was pretty crowded in light of the holiday - but tons of chairs everywhere), pool drinks a bit weak and overpriced and pool food not so great at all, the Revive spa was excellent (and i've spa'd at tons of places...def worth it to use the facilities. to escape the crowd that sunday we got a couples massage, i got a facial and we used their private pool and facilities, way less crowded), a quick walk across the street (10 mins) gets you to a great mall and outdoor food/shopping area (hit up Albertsons for drinks and snacks to save you from the pool side menu) - some say too far to walk but i disagree, the gym is nice and not crowded when we were there, have a drink on the lower level lobby at dusk, the in room lotion is from the spa so its great stuff (got the boyfriend to ask for extra!), take a walk at night around the grounds and lay on a lounge to look at the stars, and have the Transtyle sedan pick you up at the airport ($50 - and they make no other stops unlike the other shuttle services) and for the trip back to the airport do the same but ask for the shuttle that gets you on the hour ($15 and we got the same exact car .. wondering what shuttle means)...oh, and late checkout is pretty late so stretch it if you have a later flight like we did!a few odd things - house keeping came pretty late in the day and forgot turndown service both nights despite personal requests (not sure if she was just too busy), heard the pool ran out of towels for a little while during the day (we got there by around 11am so not a problem for us), the room is so-so for a 5 star hotel...finally, go to expedia for air and hotel - we got a good deal (spent more on food and spa services!)

<Author>UKtog
<Content>A stay of two halves Had I written this review after day 2 of my four night stay, the result probably would have been 5 stars as I could have tolerated some of the early slip ups, however, I made a mistake and stayed on over the Labour Day Weekend. My husband and I stayed for four nights and paid to upgrade ourselves to a Cloud Room. Well in advance (ie 3 weeks), reservations were made for all four restuarants with specific requests for outdoor seating. On arrival we were greeted well by many people and thought we were onto a winner here although it did take us some time to attract the attention of the gentleman at the Cloud Room to gain admission. Our first nights meal at Roys was exceptional with excellent attentive service; our room was beautiful and our walk in the gardens delightful. Day Two went well until Dinner, when we were seated in a corridor at Blue Sage (the dining room was empty) advised no outside seating was available (though tables were visible) and served our entree four minutes after our appetizer - the server could not understand we were not ready for it so left it anyway. Next day our problems started with the Cloud Room - this has the potential to be a great facility and the staff really do try their best. However, for Appetizers read - lovely food but used as Childrens Teas and dinner by those too mean to pay for it elsehwere. On one day there were 12 children racing around the room and others shouting and crying - one parent even pushed in ahead of us to get the last of an appetizer as it all was l her little darling would eat - we had to go without. The staff advised they have no control over the number of children in the roomas any guest in a cloud room can bring in unlimited children to the room free - so it is not a quiet oasis of calm for a pre dinner drink - quite the opposite. Breakfast was even worse as one dear child was in training for the Muffin Throwing at the Olympics event much to the amusement (and encouragement) of their parents. Obviously the hotel is not responsible for the behaviour of the parents, but be warned on the marketing, this is not the quiet facility you might think you are paying for.Contrast that with our lovely well cooked, romantic meal outdoors at the Tuscany where incidentally delightful well mannered child sat at the next table to us. Wildfire was also a good spot, though again that evening our pre dinner drinks were a shambles as the kids had empty all the adult mixers and Perrier from the fridge and the staff had to get more brought up - and when the first lot arrived doting grandparents took all the water bottles for the children. The poor assistant was so frustrated as he tried to get our preferred drinks to us. Other lapses that needed addressing were, a 50 minute wait for the (wrong) food order at the pool, with no supervisor available to register a complaint - an offer of free drinks was made but as we were about to drive and did not want alcohol or desserts that was worthless. Also had to point out every single day we were in a Cloud Room so should not be charged for parking, yet the charge still appeared on the final account; newspapers were not delivered on two of the days and each day we had to call housekeeping about things missing from our room (like the trashbin). Yes, some of these are minor grumbles, and many of the staff did work hard to provide a very good personal service, but the hotel let itself down too many times during our stay for us to rate it any higher. On check out, the lady adjusted the parking costs but was not interested in our issues re the Cloud Room (which its staff had suggested we raise with them as it concerned them too) - as we were on a tight timescale to get our flight it was pointless pursuing them, but my advice think very very carefully about spending $100 a night for a Cloud Room if you are a couple wanting a more relaxed atmosphere to sit have pre dinner drinks or breakfast in. I do hope this hotel can get its act together consistently - rather than some of the time for some of the guests

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This is the place... When Hurricane Frances decided to go to Florida the same time we were planning to be there we made some quick changes and headed West to the JW Desert Ridge in Phoenix. It turned out to be one of the best getaway weekends my wife and I have taken. It's never any fun going home after one of these weekends. Everything you needed and wanted was there on the property. Golf, the pools (including a lazy river), the restaurants and bar, all added to this incredible resort. Great restaurants and shopping were less than a mile away. We day-tripped to Sedona and further north to the Grand Canyon, all within a good full days time. The resort set us up on a great horseback ride in the desert with a very professional and friendly outfit, Canyon Creek Ranch...I couldn't imagine going back and using someone else, these guys are great. The staff at the resort were very friendly and attentive to any of our needs, the rooms very great, clean with very comfortable beds and pillows, huge bathrooms, and all rooms had a great view of something.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>About Par Decidedly ho-hum. A place like this sets high standards and it misses on most counts. Strange how people can go to the same place and come away with a different opinion, but there's no question my wife and I were disappointed after a recent visit here. Ok, yeah it was a weekend and crowded with families and kids, as many Arizona resorts are in the summer -- thanks to off season rates and priceline. But even if you're only paying $39.95 a nite you should treat the place better than a Red Roof Inn. We saw guests lugging huge personal coolers to their rooms and even out by the pools. Little kids ran around unsupervised through the lobby and hallways. Underage (and unsupervised) kids were also jumping into the spas.Of course families taking over resorts is now commonplace and when you have a huge property like Desert Ridge it's understandable to keep the rooms full. What's funny, though, is that there are any number of other resorts in the Phoenix area with better family-oriented activities, pools, slides, games and so on. In fact, there are better places period. The Desert Ridge is far out of town cut into freshly-bladed desert and not especially convenient to anything. The place is huge and unattractive from the outside-- we thought it was a prison or a government building at first. There are other resorts that have better views and are more intimate and charming. Our standard room was smallish and appointed with only fairly humdrum furnishings. No doubt there are nicer rooms, but I like to judge a place by its standard room. The restaurants were fine and not too expensive for this kind of place -- we ate at the Blue Sage and Roys (Roys was more interesting) -- but nothing gourmet. In short, the phrase that comes to mind after a visit to the Desert Ridge is fair to middling. Probably fine for a business meeting, maybe fine for a family, but there are much better places at the 5 star level in Phoenix.

<Author>candaceg
<Content>Fabulous stay at the Desert Ridge resort I was at the resort August 22-26 for a conference. The hotel was completely sold out and during the day the conference facility was serving an additional 1000 people. Despite that, the service and facilities at the hotel were outstanding. I had no complaints about my stay. Having a small refrigerator in the room was a nice touch, especially since you can come nowhere close to getting cool water from the tap! I also appreciated the power outlet inside the in-room safe so I was able to charge my laptop and have it secured. As others have mentioned, the staff is extremely friendly. The pools were great - I loved the lazy river. Since I was on eastern time, I would have liked it if the pools opened a bit earlier in the morning so I could get some laps in, but that is a minor complaint. Regarding the airport transportation - there is a shuttle service you can book through the concierge desk that is $15 a person - it's called the TransStyle shuttle.

<Author>Kendie
<Content>Best choice we could have made! We stayed at the hotel August 14 thru 18, 2004. The off season rates attracted us, but the excellent service and beautiful resort will bring us back if we are in the Phoenix area again!. Staff was very helpful and friendly, the hotel was clean and rooms were nicely furnished. The grounds and pools were wonderfully landscaped and maintained. Since we were only there for four nights, we ate all our meals at the hotel. Breakfast at Blue Sage was the best meal of the day. Dinner there was not outstanding. We also ate at the steakhouse and Roy's. Both were good, but pricey, as is to be expected at a resort of this caliber. The hotel is designed with large upper and lower level lobby areas that provide places to sit and enjoy conversation or quiet time reading. There was a convention there during our stay, but since the resort is so large, we really didn't feel crowded.We would definitely recommend a stay at this resort!

<Author>RCDC52
<Content>Off season a good option My wife and I stayed four nights during the first week of August. We made the choice based on favorable tripadvisor ratings and an unbelievable package deal we received on a last minute booking.Service and staff were first rate and very attentive.They were well below capacity during the first couple of days, although it became crowded toward the end. The resort is huge and has ample space to handle large groups of people but it was a more relaxed experience, especially around the pools when less busy. Roy's was a very good restarant, especially for seafood lovers. The Blue Sage was typical hotel fare. Decent food but a limited menu. Ditto the pool food service. Didn't eat at Tuscany. We were offered an unadvertised 3 spa treatments for the price of 2. They wound up giving us the most expensive one for free ($180 vs. $120 for the other 2) which was surprising. The facilities are very nice and having the run of the more quiet spa pool and building for the day a nice extra. My wife and I agreed the treatments were wonderful. Played the Faldo (the other is a slightly more difficult Palmer design) and found it of average difficulty depending on the tees you use. It was in pretty rough shape, but it must be difficult to keep a desert course in shape this time of year. The grounds and lobby are beautiful and designed to keep you cool even in the heat of summer. In the evening they actually air condition the patio lounge by opening the huge double doors to the lobby. It really made a difference . Always ice water on hand. It was a great choice for a romantic getaway even though it may not cater to that crowd as much as the Scottsdale resorts. The only complaint has little to do with the property itself. It cost us $100 including gratuity to travel from the airport and back using super shuttle on the way out and their much more convenient car service back to the airport. It is over 20 miles away so I wouldn't expect a complimentary shuttle, but that seemed a ridiculous amount. Seems like there should be a better otion for those who don't want to leave the resort during their stay and therefore don't need a car rental. Otherwise had a great time and would recommend the JW Marriott Desert Ridge to anyone looking for a great resort experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful relaxing vacation We spent four nights at the Desert Ridge resort at the end of July. Everyone thought we were crazy to leave the hot Kansas summer for an even hotter Arizona summer. But we are so glad we went! The staff at the resort were wonderful. We had four teenagers with us. We asked the front desk if they had any larger rooms available. They searched and found a conference room which was very large! It had a king size murphy bed, sofa, leather chairs, dining room table, bar and an extra large bathroom. We were in heaven! They brought us three very comfortable cots for the kid to sleep on. We had planned to spend a day of our vacation driving to Sedona and on to the Grand Canyon, but after the first hour at the resort we decided we didn't want to leave. It was a perfect place to vacation. Wonderful shopping close by, Beautiful gardens everywhere,very relaxing pools plus my husband had a great time golfing for two days. Again the service was by far the best we have ever experienced. The heat didn't bother us at all, I guess it's true that without the humidity it doesn't feel so hot. When we were in the shade it was quite pleasant. I definitely want to go back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Enthusiastic Staff My wife and I stayed here over the fourth of July weekend. The staff was by far and away the most enthusiastic we have ever encountered in any hotel. We received greetings from six separate employees from the time we stepped out of our car and got to the check in desk, a distance of perhaps fifty feet. (Over-staffed?)We got a great rate on Priceline and perhaps that's why we were given the absolutely farthest room (1180) from the lobby, pools, and main gathering area. We dropped off our bags and went to orient ourselves with the facilities and when we found out how far away we were from everything, we asked for a room change. I had non-chalantly asked one of the hotel employees about occupancy and learned that it was only about 60% so we thought we had a pretty good chance. Our room was changed promptly to building block 4 which is much closer to everything but they wouldn't give us a view overlooking the main courtyard. Instead, we were given a view of the Desert Botanical Garden. Not bad, but I would have preferred the courtyard view.We noticed that in our second room there were no bathrobes as was in the first room. Housekeeping brought them up to us. Also, we learned that they don't stock stationary as a standard item, you have to ask and they will bring it to you. We found a convenient laundry room in our block of rooms. The washers and dryers are free with detergent and softener supplied as well.For dinner on both nights we ate at Roy's. We dropped by the restaurant in the afternoon before they start serving to check out the menu and Bob the managing partner was extremely friendly and allowed us to poke around. The Hawaiian fusion food is fantastic. The best deal is the prix fixe menu. For $30 you get an appetizer your choice of entree and dessert. The next night we ate off the sushi menu. Mako, the chef partner, definitely knows what he's doing. We sat outdoors the first night and inside the second. Sitting outside is definitely better. The tiki torches add to the ambiance.There's a Starbucks inside the main area. Get a coupon for a free tall coffee of the day by going to the timeshare desk. The timeshare people aren't there at 6:00 am so make sure to get the coupon during the day. Just tell them you're only interested in the free coffee and they'll lay off the hard sell. If you prefer to drink something else, they give you a dollar off any dring with the coupon. Also, at Starbucks, bring your water bottle and fill it up with free water that includes lemon and strawberry accents. Later on in the day you can really taste the fruit as it settles into the water.Valet parking is $17 per day so you may want to think about self parking except it's a long hike back. A shuttle from the parking lot would be nice to see.My wife went to the spa and got the 80 minute stone massage ($180 + tip). She was content although it might have been a little expensive. The service was good and the facilities tranquil and relaxing.Overall, this is quite a resort we would definitely visit again when in the Phoenix area.

<Content>Absolutely the best! Two night stay--- June 30 - July 2This is an incredible resort hotel that caters to professionals, (the bellmen said about 70% business) and their families that join them! We were thrilled with our vacation! We were not there on business, so we just used their pools and lazy river to catch some fun in the sun! We experienced no crowds at all in the water, in fact we marveled that about 95% of the chairs were empty all day around their pools. Now, we did drop a bit of money at their Blue Sage restaurant and Roy's, but we knew we would. Our daughter was tired of the same old kids menu items, so we requested that a small bean/cheese burrito and side of rice be made at Blue Sage--- no problem at all, they were happy to oblige. We have traveled widely and found this hotel to be top notch. I think you will enjoy your stay!Families, ask for a room in the 4000 wing-- the views are amazing!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Week at the Marriott My wife and I stayed at the resort from June 5-10, 2004 for a visiting conference. We both *loved* the resort, from the beautiful grounds to the excellent dinners at Blue Sage and Roy's. We spent our first day at the Revive Spa. We were able to enjoy the private pool area for many hours (until 8pm) away from the kids and crowds at the other pools (which weren't very crowded, but there were only a few others at the spa pool). The lobby is beautiful at night. We enjoyed sitting outside on the lounge chairs and outdoor couches, looking up at the pools with the firepits around us, sipping on drinks from the bar. Phoenix weather is also something to behold - we didn't see a cloud for 5 days and the nights were warm, but not hot. Perfect for late night strolls around the grounds. Our room was also great, with a private balcony and turn down service twice a day. The bathrooms are beautiful. Service was top notch. The staff was very nice. There is a car service to the mall across the street for $5, or it's a quick 15 minute walk (time of day is the key of making the choice to walk or get a ride.) I used the fitness facilities twice, which are adequate. If your body is on east coast time, you'll be treated to early morning sunrises across the back of the resort earlier than 5am. The gardens around the resort and water features are gorgeous. The only possible negative of the resort is that from the distance, it doesn't look like much. You can only really see the palm trees in the front and since it expands out to the north, you only see the southern stucco wings from the road. From the highway, it's even hard to pick out the resort, so the resort doesn't look like the oasis it is from a distance. However, once you drive up to resort and walk in the lobby and see the grounds, you immediately know it's a special place. We would definitely return.   
<Date>Jun 14, 2004

<Author>sullgreg
<Content>Highest Praise for the Desert Ridge Reort and Spa! My family spent spring break at the new JW Marriott DEsert Ridge Resort and Spa in April. We have been to a number of wonderful hotels around the country, and none of us can wait to return to this hotel. We stayed in one of the Cloud Club rooms, which gave us access to additional amenities. If it is within your budget, the additional cost is well worth the level of service and amenities (such as full breakfast, snacks and beverages throughout the day, evening appetizers and full open bar, and dessert, including specialized concierge services) provided, and the Cloud Club staff could not be more helpful. The recreational offerings include several pools and a river pool, with a slide, that was great fun for us and for our teenage daughter and her friend. Golf courses and services were first-rate. The spa, which includes a terrific (and quiet!) pool as well as a spa restaurant, offered excellent massages. We were less impressed with the manicure/pedicure services offered in the salon, which were overpriced and lesser quality. Rooms were spacious, with balconies, and the hotel staff was attentive; on the occasions that we made a special request, we received immediate service. We at at Roy's and the Blue Sage (breakfast and dinner) and found both to be extremely high quality, with exceptional service. The appetizers that we sampled from the other hotel restaruants were excellent, as well. I would highly recommend using the hotel's vacation planning services (check the hotel web site) in advance of your visit; we did, and we received wonderful recreational, dining and cultural recommendations and had all reservations made for us prior to our arrival. If you are looking for a bargain, this hotel is not for you. If you are looking for an upscale, high-quality experience, with impressive retaurants, spa, and recreation, make your reservation now!

<Content>Great Summer Prices - Fun Resort I stayed at the brand-new resort in June 2003. I live in Phoenix, just 4 miles from the resort, and received a fantastic $99.00 a night rate, plus discounts on the spa. I invited 3 girlfriends to share a room with two double beds with me (you can have up to 5 people per room for no extra charge, so the room cost $25.00 plus 1/4 tax per night). We stayed for two evenings (Friday and Saturday nights), and had a blast. The resort is absolutely beautiful. The pool and water features are fantastic. The spa is wonderful, and the staff there treats you like a celebrity. The spa is gorgeous, with its own pool and the spa services are excellent. For visitors from out of town: for dining, go across the street to the Desert Ridge outdoors mall. The prices are MUCH better. There are a number of excellent restaurants; nightclubs; shopping and an AMC theater, all within walking distance (right across the street from the resort). Restaurants include Macaroni Grill; Friday's; Bahama Breeze; On the Border; Malee's; and much more, serving any kind of food you desire. Ray's restaurant at the resort is excellent, but VERY pricey. Ditto for the resort bar: you'll pay about $10.00 per drink. Go across the street and drink and eat for MUCH less. There's also an Albertson's grocery store across the street for munchies, toiletries, drinks and more.

<Content>Grand hotel in the desert This hotel, given its size is one of the best I have ever stayed in. The only reason that I didn't give it an excellent review was the size.. but when I asked my kids aged 12 and 8 they didnt waver in their love of the hotel. The pool area was too crowded for my liking ( even though the service was quick , friendly and efficient) but there was so much pool there was never a problem getting a chair. The lazy river was nice, my kids koved it , but I was expecting a more exotic setting for that after reading the reviews , so I was a little dissapointed. The Cloud club was amazing, well worth theprice, . The spa was beautiful and the massages were good . Check in was fast friendly and stressless. The hotel could use a more casual restaurant and perhaps some nighttime entertainment.Roys is a great restaurant. The tennis program needs to be developed and is too pricey.The service and staff though not a trained as Ritz Carlton staff was great and I have never met people so willing to make my stay pleasant , especailly at the cloud club level.I will definitely return ..especially with my kids. If I want a quiet getaway without thekids though ,I might think twice and go to a smaller more intimate place..

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Comfortable, beautiful hotel in Phoenix The Marriot Desert Ridge was a beautiful, comfortable hotel. We were pleasantly surprised at how great an experience we had at such a large hotel, since we tend to prefer smaller, boutique hotels. But despite it's large size (the largest resort hotel in Phoenix with over 900 rooms!) we never felt too overwhelmed or lost. The rooms were very large and comfortable, the service was fantastic. The food was average, except for Roy's which was terrific. We spent the extra money for the Cloud Club which was very nice, but I'm not sure if it was really worth it for us. The pools were great and the spa was absolutely wonderful! The location is a bit far from everything since it's in the very northern part of Phoenix, and right next to a large shopping area. But you really don't feel the need to leave the property and could probably manage just staying there. Overall, very nice and somewhere I would consider staying again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely beautiful! Just returned from this beautiful resort! We were looking for a last minute getaway with our 18 month old son and chose this based on other great reviews from Trip Advisor. We were not disappointed! We went for 4 days and were treated with great service from the moment we stepped out of the car. Standard rooms are good sized with big bathrooms and both tub and separate shower. The resort is sparkling...almost brand new with beautiful tennis, golf, spa and pool facilities. They have fountains everywhere (even one that small children can play in near the pools). We were unlucky with weather for the first few days but were able to find some great side trips (Sedona and the Phoenix Zoo) until it was time to lay poolside. The lazy river and waterslide were great as well as several other standard pools. Restaurants are better than room service which had limited choices. We had an extravagant breakfast buffet included with our room which was the highlight meal of each day. Also, great food at Roy's restaurant where they welcomed our toddler... surprisingly kid friendly, especially for a fine restaurant. Major THUMBS UP on JW Marriott Desert Ridge.

<Author>ushma
<Content>Simply Fabulous The JW Marriott Desert Ridge Resort and Spa was beautiful. It's only about a year old so it's in great shape. We were in Phoenix for a New Year's getaway. We were first at the Marriott Camelback but we moved mid-stay to see what else was out there. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Cloud Club a heavenly experience Wow, what a place! Two college friends and I went for a long girls weekend to celebrate our 40th birthdays. We splurged on the Cloud Club level accommodations. We were met at the airport by a town car (complimentary) and whisked away to the resort, where we were treated like royalty from the minute we walked in the door. Our room was very nice, but not huge. Marble bathroom, cd player- in all, nicely appointed. We enjoyed the many pools, and spent two full days hanging out at the Revive Spa, where we swam, ate lunches, enjoyed treatments (massages, facials, lime salt body scrubs) and took our sweet time showering and fixing ourselves up for our evening activities. In the Cloud Club Sky Lounge, we were treated to wonderful cooked to order breakfasts, fabulous coffee, open bar from 5-10 every night, hors' d'ouevres from 5-6 (along with a chef who explained what he was cooking for us), and wonderful desserts from 8-10 each evening. Ken, our personal Cloud Club Guardian Angel, took such good care of us. When we jokingly complained about the lack of good (read, 80's) music in the club, he went home that evening and burned cd's more to our liking. The requested music was playing softly for us when we came in for coffee the next morning at 7:00. This is but one example of the pampering we received at Desert Ridge.I highly recommend this facility- we'll be going back next spring!
